> see Sources. "What this game is / Eras /
> Core entities / Glossary" describe the **shipped build** (cited `file:line`).
> The gap log is grouped by area; each row is tagged `ingested` (forum-cited) or
> `codebase`, and notes when a delta is **corroborated across multiple eras** (the
> strongest signal that it is real and load-bearing). A separate **Confirmed
> shipped bugs** subsection lists defects (fixes, not features). The `modern`
> thread is the most mechanically *mature* source; the `house-divided` thread is
> the most mechanically *unique* (1856-native, Civil War / Reconstruction); the
> **`drums` thread is the most mechanically *interior*** — an **all-CPU** run that
> exposes CPU heuristics, thresholds, tie-breaks, and design-holes that prior
> multiplayer threads couldn't capture; **`pop` is the most mechanically
> *initialized*** — the **first fresh-boot of a modern-era scenario** (the
> **scenario-boot model**, gap-log #86); and **`rep1800` is the most
> mechanically *foundational*** — it **fills the entire 1800–1856 early-republic
> gap** (Jeffersonian → Era-of-Good-Feelings → Jacksonian → Manifest-Destiny, an
> era band with NO prior coverage) AND establishes the **★ headline architecture
> finding: eras are content-bands gated by game-state + territory ownership, NOT
> calendar year** (gap-log #92), contradicting the shipped `year % 4` era model.
> **★ Batch 8 makes #92 the single most-corroborated architectural finding in the
> KB: MULTI-SAVE CONFIRMED.** Two fully-independent saves — `tea1772` (1772 start)
> and `rep1800` (1800 start, 28 in-game years apart) — emit the **identical
> era-band labels** (Federalists → Republicanism → Democracy → Manifest-Destiny →
> Nationalism) **at the same in-game dates**, proving the bands are deterministic
> game-state content-gates, not flavor or per-thread GM invention (`tea1772` §2 /
> POST 21, 62, 91, 130, 153; `rep1800` POST 92, 6201). Batch 8 also delivers the
> **first multiplayer 1772** (`new1772`) — confirming the entire founding-era
> apparatus (inaugural draft, Continental/Constitutional Convention, Revolutionary
> War, era-event graph, offices-stood-up-by-law) from a MULTI-FACTION angle, not
> just the batch-2 solo thread. **★ Negative result:** no thread in the corpus
> reaches a "future" era — `tea1772` stalls at 1874 (mid-Gilded) despite its title
> — so "Era of the Future" remains undocumented everywhere (open question).
> The core loop is now **corroborated across 5+ eras / 11 threads**.
>
> **★ Batch 9 (`nuke`) covers the Cold-War / modern HALF (1948→~2005)** — the
> single largest corpus, and the direct predecessor of the batch-3 `modern`
> (2004→2020) thread (read them as one 1948→2020 campaign; the seam is the 2004
> election). Five headlines: (1) **the #92 era-band model now holds across a THIRD
> start year (1948)** — confirmed across **1772 / 1800 / 1948** — and is **refined
> into TWO LEVELS**: point-banked **Historical Eras** (here "Nuclear Age" 1948–2000
> → "Era of Terror" 2000–~2012) vs **decade/census boundaries WITHIN an era** (1972/
> 1980/1990 = bulk EV reallocation + wholesale state-bias re-lean + content rotation).
> **The earlier-extractor "Era of Neocons" band was a MISLABEL — it is a FACTION
> REBRAND + a decade content-rotation, NOT a point-banked band** (logged so it is
> not re-introduced; #92). (2) **The "Cold War" is NOT a system** — it is the
> generic naval→land war engine RELABELED + event-flavor; **no nuclear/MAD/NATO/
> space-race subsystem, no army/navy/air branches, wars never resolve, and the USSR
> NEVER FALLS** (the dissolution chain stalls at a ~5% gate; still a named ally in
> 2005). (3) **The realignment is mechanically-but-GRADUALLY enforced** (4 cooperating
> levers, "1964→early-1990s"), NOT a single scripted flip — and BLUE/RED meaning
> **flips DURING the game** (Dixiecrats start INSIDE Blue). (4) **The ideology scale
> is a CIRCLE** (LW-Pop↔RW-Pop adjacent at 25%) — independently CORROBORATED from a
> SECOND thread (POST 9842; was #99 from `rep1800`). (5) This is the **fullest modern-
> systems capture in the KB** (the primary→brokered-convention→general machine, the
> diplomacy subsystem, first impeachment/resignation/unelected-succession, legislated-
> variable SCOTUS, mutable cabinet, Era-of-Terror content). **★ And the strongest
> corpus statement of design intent: the digital APP is built for 1-human-vs-9-CPU**
> (multiplayer "goes off the rails"), even though `nuke` itself is ~7–10-human MP —
> validating the roadmap's solo-first sequencing (#114). The thread breaks at 2005;
> the **seam to the successor `modern` (2004→2020) is the next likely batch.**
>

> Era-of-Good-Feelings → Jacksonian "Era of Democracy"), 10-human MP, **GA'd by

> the playtests are the design source of truth: mid-thread the engine designer

> **`drums` reconfirms this theme:** mid-thread `vcczar`/`Tyler` patched the CPU

> (POST 7406). The build must absorb these patches.

## ★ North-star: the app must subsume the human GM

**AMPU's core engineering mandate is a zero-human-GM game.** Every playtest and
discussion thread in this corpus is run by a human Game Master (usually
MrPotatoTed / vcczar) who, turn after turn, performs work *by hand* that the
shipped build does not yet do. **Every GM hand-adjudication recorded in these
digests is, by definition, a feature the shipped game must perform
automatically and deterministically** (seeded RNG, `src/rng.ts` — never a human
die-roll or a raw `Math.random`). The gap log below is, read correctly, the
catalogue of exactly that work.

The GM is doing **two distinct jobs**, and the game must own **both**:

**① GM as referee / calculator** — the rules math and machinery the GM computes
by hand each turn. This is the half that is *least* visible in a casual read of
the corpus, and the one the batch-27 `redbutton` platform finding surfaced
(a 492-40 landslide caused by the GM mis-applying a `+1` as `+3`; the platform
"engine" does not exist in code — it is GM arithmetic). It must move into the
deterministic engine:

| GM computes by hand | Must become engine | Gaps |
|---|---|---|
| Election/platform scoring, the swing die, historical-bias terms | The election scorer owns the math; UI shows only player-visible numbers ("fog of war") | #184, DH-72, #18, #14, QW3, **QW19–QW21** |
| Primary → brokered-convention: delegate weights, balloting, walkouts, kingmaker VP | A convention state-machine | #185, #183, #19, #20 |
| Scenario boot: year-correct incumbents, seeded delegates, back-dated careers, retro-fatigue | A deterministic per-year `BootSheet` (incl. mid-cycle/late-era shape) | #186, #187, #86, #115, #173 |
| Cabinet meter rolls / lingering effects | A lingering-roll engine | #179 |
| Treaty / decision-event / diplomacy adjudication, retry budgets | Era decision-event spine + treaty→territory + bounded retries | #177, #178, #107, #162 |
| End-condition tracking (incl. the "big red button" nuclear loss) | Meter-floor game-end model | #88, #188 |
| Explaining the rules so players don't need a GM to interpret them | In-app rules surface | DH-69, QW21 |

> **★ Charter metric (batch 33, `excelautomate` — the build-side burden budget):**
> the spreadsheet-era GM stated an explicit, dated **GM-burden budget — *">30 min/
> phase ⇒ must automate"*** (POST 59: *"if any phase is still taking me more than 30
> minutes to process, that's a phase I'll focus on automating further"*), with the
> aspirational end-state that once the math is automated *"updating [the History tab]
> will become the only time-consuming part of this game"* (POST 10). The same thread
> is the cleanest itemized inventory of the ① referee/calculator load and its lived
> automation-PRIORITY order: **(1) seat tallies → (2) per-politician trait/eligibility
> lookup → (3) per-office election scoring → (4) legislative-package point scoring**.
> Tellingly, the two tasks the GM *couldn't* automate in Excel — **term-limit history-
> counting** and **per-candidate die rolls** — are exactly the two the app handles
> trivially (office tenure in `snap`; seeded `rng.ts`): the hardest manual GM tasks
> are the engine's easiest. This is the concrete, quantified statement of the §①
> mandate — corroborates **#114 / DH-36** from the build side (`excelautomate` POST 1,
> 10, 52, 59).

**② GM as opponent** — the GM also *plays* every non-human faction (in solo
runs, all 9). This half the docs already headline hard:

| GM does by hand | Must become engine | Gaps |
|---|---|---|
| Per-faction CPU decisions: candidate selection, voting, meter management, cabinet/legislative heuristics | The **E9 handler suite + K5 `CpuController`** (today `grep runCpuFaction\|perFactionSim src/` = ZERO) | #114, E9, K5, CPU-AI spec cluster #70–#78 |
| (cost of NOT having it) | — | **DH-36** — 4 documented GM-burnout playtest deaths |

**The single most-corroborated cross-batch lesson** in the corpus is that the
manual CPU-faction simulation + opaque rules are what *kill* playtests (burnout
on the build side, confusion on the player side), and that the only runs to reach
a natural endpoint did so because the **designer personally absorbed the GM load**
(batch-25 `principle1772`: a 1-human-vs-9-CPU game completed *only* because Ted
hand-simulated all 9 CPU factions to ~1800). That is precisely the work ① + ②
above must remove from the human.

> **Going-forward convention (digests + gap log):** when a digest records the GM
> doing something by hand, tag it **`GM⇒App`** and ensure it has (or gets) a
> gap-log row. A `GM⇒App` item is never "designer flavor" to leave to a human —
> it is an automation requirement. The roadmap's **"GM-replacement" lens**
> (`roadmap.md`) groups these into a buildable program; the technical-guide
> (`technical-guide.md` §9) sequences them.

## What this game is

AMPU is a turn-based American political strategy game that runs in the browser
(React + TypeScript + Vite; state persists in IndexedDB). The player runs a
**faction** inside one of two parties (BLUE / RED) and steers it across a
historical timeline: draft politicians, develop them, win elections, staff the
government, pass legislation, fight wars, and resolve era-defining decision
events. There is no single win screen baked in for both scenarios; play is a
campaign across a sequence of phases per turn, with terminal endings on certain
era events (`GameState.gameEnded`, `EraEvent.triggersGameEnd`, types.ts:1476,
1635).

As shipped, AMPU is **single-player**: the human owns exactly one faction
(`Faction.isPlayer`, types.ts:1303; `playerFactionId`, types.ts:1566) and the
engine drives every other faction as CPU. The turn loop is a fixed **phase
sequence** of ~36 phases grouped into 10 categories (`PHASE_SEQUENCE`,
phases.ts:3-47), advanced two years at a time (`nextPhaseInfo` adds 2 per turn
rollover, phases.ts:161). Most systems are **pure functions over a single
`FullGameSnapshot`** (types.ts:1811) in `src/engine/`; the UI is a registry of
~35 pages (registry.ts) with no router.

The engine is deterministic by design (seeded RNG, `src/rng.ts`) and the phase
taxonomy is numbered ("2.1.1 Politician Draft", "2.9.4 Presidential Election",
…) — the same taxonomy the forum game uses, so this build is recognizably an
implementation of that game.

The player's goal is open-ended faction-building: accumulate Political Value
(PV) across your politicians, control offices (Presidency, Congress, governors,
cabinet, courts), shape national meters and interest-group standing, and survive
/ steer the era's crises. **PV drives elections** (`src/pv.ts`; CLAUDE.md).

## Eras & scenarios

The codebase has **four era values** — `independence`, `federalism`,
`nationalism`, `modern` (`Era`, types.ts:1337) — but only **two shipped
scenarios**, and only **three eras are reachable in play**. The forum runs a
**continuous multi-era campaign** (a 1772 or 1800 start runs straight through
independence → federalism → nationalism → gilded → …), with **points reset at
each era boundary** (federalism digest post 518). Eras are not just flavor: each
is a balance dimension *and* carries its own faction roster, nickname table,
draft-ideology profile, era-event spine, bill catalog, card pool, and SCOTUS
case set.

| Scenario | Start | Era(s) reachable | Defining issues | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **1772 — Founding** | 1772, era `independence` (scenario1772.ts:97) | `independence` → `federalism` on Constitution ratification (constitutionalConvention.ts:198) | Independence vs. loyalty, the Revolutionary War, confederation vs. federal union, writing the Constitution | **Built** |
| **1788 — Early Republic** | 1788, era `federalism` | `federalism` (1788–1800) → `nationalism` at ~1800 | **Hamilton vs. Jefferson**: assume Rev-War debt, Bank of the US, US Mint, tariff (set to 10%), bimetallic currency, Militia Act; Compromise of 1790; Whiskey/Fries rebellions; **party-formation as era events** (~1792); French-Revolution wars (War of 1795, Barbary); per-state shift to popular-vote electors; state-by-state slavery abolition vs. Cotton Gin; Louisiana Purchase | **Designed, not built** — now richly documented (federalism digest is the spec) |
| **1800 → Nationalism (the `rep1800` arc, 1800→1868)** | continuous campaign, mid-government boot (`BLUE = Dem-Republicans`, `RED = Federalists→National Republicans` — **party frame inverted** vs later eras) | Forum-internal sub-bands of `nationalism`: **Republicanism (1800–20) → Democracy (1820–40) → Manifest Destiny (1840–56) → Nationalism (1856–68)**; eras advance on **game-state, not year** (#92) | **Republicanism:** British impressment vs France, 12th-Amendment unlock, the 2nd Bank + tariff. **Democracy (Jacksonian):** universal white-male suffrage, the **Bank War**, internal improvements, tariff, slavery. **Manifest Destiny:** Pacific expansion, Texas/Mexican-Cession, slavery-cannot-expand, SC secession threat, Catholic-immigration nativism. **Nationalism:** alt-Civil-War (Pres defects to CSA, UK intervention, guerrilla phase) → Reconstruction | **Designed, not built** — the `rep1800` digest is the spec; **fills the previously-uncovered 1800–1856 gap**. Predecessor of the `gilded` (1868) arc; the 1800 campaign is now documented end-to-end |
| **1856 — Antebellum** | 1856, era `nationalism` (scenario1856.ts:177) | **Shipped:** `nationalism` only (spine ends at the Trent Affair, 1861). **Designed (`hd`):** the same start runs **continuously 1856→1904+** through Nationalism → Gilded (1868) → Progressivism (1892) | Slavery, popular sovereignty / free soil, sectional crisis, **secession & Civil War → Reconstruction** — then forward into the tariff/currency/civil-service/imperialism Gilded issues and the Progressive issue-space | **Partially built** — the antebellum *start* ships, but the **Civil-War combat engine, Reconstruction subsystem, secession-trait gating, sectional-balance crisis, and Canada/era-continuation** are designed-not-built (`hd` digest is the spec; gap rows #56–#69) |
| **1800 → Gilded Age (1868–1892)** | continuous campaign | Reaches a `gilded`-style era (likely the `modern` enum, or its own value) | **Tariff** (national integer set by legislation); **currency** (Gold-Standard vs Bimetallism/Free Silver); **civil-service reform / anti-corruption** ("Honest Gov't" crisis); **imperialism** (island naval bases); Native-relations bills; Chinese / Jewish immigration bans; women's suffrage (state-by-state); Jim Crow / Poll Tax / Prohibition policy switches | **Designed, not built** — confirmed by the gilded digest |
| **1948 → Modern (the `nuke`+`modern` arc — one campaign family 1948→2020)** | a **1948 mid-20th-c. boot** (the `nuke` thread runs 1948→~2005; `modern` continues 2004→2020) | The full **`modern`** era, split into the two-level era model: point-banked Historical Eras **"Nuclear Age" (1948–2000) → "Era of Terror" (2000–~2012) → Populism (2012–2024)**, with per-decade census boundaries (1972/1980/1990) inside each | **Most mechanically mature era.** Modern issue menu (tariff power to the President, income-tax brackets, healthcare, immigration, climate, Wall Street, gun control, surveillance/drone/detention); the **named meter bank + enthusiasm/Party-Pref engine**; **full primary→brokered-convention→general** subsystem; **named-Justice SCOTUS docket** (legislated-variable size, court-packing, compelled votes); modern legislative depth (Crisis Bills, packaging, Executive-Branch-Interference, investigations, mutable cabinet); 53-state alt roster (DC/Cuba/PR) under a Wyoming-Rule apportionment; **the realignment** (Dixiecrats inside Blue → modern polarity by ~1980); diplomacy (8 named nations); the **generic war engine relabeled** as the Cold War | **Designed, not built** — `nuke` backfills the **1948→2004 origin** (the fullest modern capture); `modern` is the 2004→2020 continuation |
| **"The next era" (post-1892, pre-modern)** | implied | unknown | Feminists, socialists, communists, prohibitionists, eugenicists, labor activists — narrated as forthcoming in the Gilded-Age era brief | **Designed, scope unclear** |

The forward arc is therefore **nationalism → gilded → progressive → … →
modern**: the `nationalism` Civil-War scenario is built, but the gilded/
progressive/modern eras at the end of the timeline are only `modern`-enum tuning
rows with no scenario. **federalism** sits *between* the two built scenarios and
is well-documented (`fed`); the **modern** end-state is now the best-documented
unbuilt era (`modern` digest — a 2276-post campaign).

**Alt-history note.** The forum campaigns are **alternate timelines**, not
re-enactments. The `modern` campaign began at **1948** and 60 in-game years of
player decisions produced a divergent present: a **53-state** union (DC, **Cuba**,
**Puerto Rico** are full states), ahistorical presidents (Cuomo, Kirk, a 3-term
Cochran), and ahistorical SCOTUS rulings (Janus/Atkins/Dobbs all decided
differently, flagged "ahistorical"). The game runs on **its own clock**, with
**fictional era names** ("Era of Terror" …–2012, "Era of Populism" 2012–2024) and
events firing ~10 years behind real tech. Real history supplies *texture and the
menu of plausible issues*; outcomes, officeholders, and the enacted-law record are
the campaign's own. (Per historical-context.md §10, the **modern era is the one
window where BLUE=Democrat=left / RED=Republican=right with no polarity caveat**,
and the shipped flat interest-group pool — Big Tech, Big Oil & Gas, Globalists,
LW/RW Media, anachronistic in 1856/1868 — **fits here**.) `modern` 426, 1080,
2067; historical-context §10.

- **1772** is a long "expansion-style" inaugural draft: the entire politician
  pool is drafted snake-order (scenario1772.ts:86, 107-117); historical founders
  enter via the CSV-driven inaugural draft, not the seed roster. It starts with
  **no government** — no president, no cabinet, no governors, no courts — which
  unlock through era events (Declaration → governors; Constitution → presidency,
  courts, cabinet). Era-event spine (eraEvents1772.ts): Intolerable Acts,
  Lexington & Concord, Continental Army, Alliance with France, Declaration of
  Independence, Articles of Confederation, Treaty of Paris, Annapolis →
  Constitutional Convention, plus westward events (Vermont, Fort Stanwix).
- **1856** starts **mid-government**: Buchanan is president, the Constitution is
  ratified, governors and courts exist (scenario1856.ts:179-193). It begins past
  the draft phase (`phaseId: '2.1.2'`, scenario1856.ts:153). Era-event spine
  (eraEvents1856.ts): Bleeding Kansas, Dred Scott, Panic of 1857, Southern
  Secession Threat, Secession Winter (1860–61), Trent Affair.
- **Era is also a balance dimension**, not just flavor: many rule tables are keyed
  by `Era` — mortality multipliers (`MORTALITY_RULES.eraConfig`, types.ts:507),
  faction-leadership churn (`LEADERSHIP_RULES.eraConfig`, types.ts:460), anytime-
  event rates (`ANYTIME_EVENTS_RULES.eraConfig`, types.ts:1076), and several
  trait election/governance effects are era-scaled. `modern` rows exist
  throughout but no shipped scenario reaches that era.

## Core entities & systems (index)

One line each; see `game-mechanics.md` for the actual rules/math.

- **Politician** (types.ts:1251) — the unit. Has `skills` (6 keys, 0–5),
  `command`, `traits[]`, `expertise[]`, `ideology`, faction/party, age, office,
  career track, PV cache, loyalty. **Drafted, never hand-placed** in 1772.
- **Skills** (types.ts:24) — `admin, legislative, judicial, military, governing,
  backroom`, integers 0–5.
- **Command** — a separate combat/leadership stat (not in `Skills`), gates
  kingmaking and military command.
- **Traits** (types.ts:62) — ~60 positive/negative tags (Charismatic, Integrity,
  Corrupt, Iron Fist, …) added over time (PR4b/PR6 batches), with symmetric
  conflict pairs (`TRAIT_CONFLICTS`, types.ts:658) and election/governance
  effects (`TRAIT_ELECTION_EFFECTS`, `TRAIT_GOVERNANCE_EFFECTS`).
- **Expertise** (types.ts:182) — a third axis, 19 policy domains (Economics,
  Foreign Affairs, Military, Labor, …), granted by office/career/lobby.
- **Ideology** (types.ts:5) — 7-point scale `LW Populist … RW Populist`; drifts
  and can be deliberately shifted.
- **Career tracks** (types.ts:43) — 7 tracks; politicians accrue skills/traits/
  expertise over up to 20 years on a track (phase 2.1.2).
- **Faction** (types.ts:1293) — what the player runs. Belongs to a party, has a
  `personality` (LW/Center/RW) and three card decks: `ideologyCards`,
  `lobbyCards`, `interestCards`. Factions drift alignment over time (phase 2.1.8).
- **Party** (types.ts:1306) — two: BLUE and RED. Meaning is **era-specific**
  (see glossary).
- **State** (types.ts:1318) — 13 colonies (states1772.ts) or 31 states
  (states1856.ts); has region, electoral votes, `bias`, `industries`, senators/
  reps/governor; 1772 colonies carry `ccDelegateSlots`/`colonySize`. The `region`
  enum already includes `Caribbean`/`Latin America`/`Pacific`/`Atlantic` — partial
  readiness for the modern 53-state alt roster (DC/Cuba/PR as states; gap-log #55).
- **Offices** (`OfficeType`, types.ts:1111) — President, VP, 7 cabinet seats
  (era-gated by year, `cabinetSeatsForYear`, types.ts:1196), General-in-Chief /
  Admiral, Chief/Associate Justice, Senator, Representative, Governor, Speaker,
  Pro Tem, Committee Chair, Faction/Party Leader, CC President, Ambassador.
- **Elections** (`calcStateVote`; `ElectionContext`, types.ts:697) — 6 contexts:
  presGeneral, presPrimary, house, senatePre17 (both eras use pre-17th-Amendment
  legislature-elected senate), governor, internalParty. PV-driven.
- **Legislation** (types.ts:1506) — factions propose bills routed to one of four
  committees (Domestic/Foreign/Economic/Justice), committee review, then House +
  Senate floor votes (phases 2.6.1–2.6.3).
- **National meters** (`NationalMeters`, types.ts:1399) — revenue, economic,
  military, domestic, honest, quality, planet; tick in the Lingering phase (2.5.1)
  and via events/legislation. The forum's modern bank adds **Party Preference**,
  **per-power relation meters** (8 powers), and **per-ideology enthusiasm** to this
  set, with crisis/cascade rules (gap-log #50).
- **Interest groups / enthusiasm / party preference** — `InterestGroupScores`,
  `Enthusiasm` (ideology×party −5..+5), `partyPreference`: the electoral mood
  substrate. The forum drives these via a formalized **4-part enthusiasm-reshuffle
  + faction-Score** engine (gap-log #51).
- **Era events** (`EraEvent`, types.ts:1466) — interactive scripted decisions
  (phase 2.4.3) with a `decider` (president/congress/cabinet/cc-president/auto)
  and effect-bearing responses; some unlock systems or end the game. 1772 also
  has a data-driven **precondition graph** (`Predicate`, types.ts:1487;
  `ERA_GRAPH_RULES`).
- **Anytime events** (phase 2.4.2) — non-scripted historical/scandal events
  (anytimeEvents.ts, anytimeNationalEvents.ts), era-rate-scaled.
- **Era systems (1772 only, in the build):** Continental Congress
  (`ContinentalCongress`, types.ts:1347; built via phase 2.9.6), Revolutionary
  War (`RevolutionaryWar`, types.ts:1371; battles in 2.7.2), Constitutional
  Convention (`ConstitutionalConvention`, types.ts:1801; sets
  `ConstitutionalArticles`). **Design intent:** war is a *generic* cross-era
  system (War of 1795, Barbary, 1812) — see gap-log #45 — and Constitutional
  change continues post-founding via durable **Amendments** (gap-log #39).
- **Player meta-systems (per-turn passes, phases 2.1.3–2.1.8):** Flip-Flopper
  cleanup, Relocations, Ideology Shifts, Faction Conversions (poaching/signing),
  Kingmakers & Protégés, Faction Personalities/Alignment drift. Each has its own
  rule const block and event feed in types.ts.
- **Cabinet & loyalty (PR5/PR6)** — cabinet appointments scored per seat
  (`CABINET_SEAT_SCORING`); 1856 cabinet members carry `loyalty` that decays in
  the Secession Winter event and can trigger defection.
- **Draft dataset** — bundled "standard draft classes" are **generated** by Node
  scripts (`scripts/`), ~18.5k politicians runtime-loaded from
  `public/standard-draft-classes.json`; users can import custom draftees
  (`ImportedDraftee`, types.ts:1780). Do not hand-edit generated files.

## Glossary

- **PV (Political Value)** — a politician's weighted worth, office-weighted;
  the currency that drives elections (`computePV`/`refreshPv`, src/pv.ts).
- **BLUE / RED** — the two parties; **meaning is era-specific.** 1772: BLUE =
  Patriots / Anti-Federalists, RED = Federalists (factions1772.ts:27-28). 1856:
  BLUE = Democratic Party, RED = Republican Party (factions1856.ts:19-22). Do not
  assume a fixed left/right reading across eras.
- **Faction personality** — `LW | Center | RW`, the faction's coarse lean;
  distinct from a politician's 7-point `ideology`.
- **Era** — engine bucket (`independence/federalism/nationalism/modern`), a
  superset of scenario; used for balance scaling, not just narrative.
- **Half-term / turn** — the loop advances 2 years per full pass of the phase
  sequence; `HalfTermSummary` (types.ts:1762) records per-turn deltas.
- **senatePre17** — election context: both shipped scenarios predate the 17th
  Amendment, so senators are chosen by state legislatures, never popular vote
  (types.ts:696-703).
- **electorsByLegislature** *(early-republic, `rep1800`)* — a proposed per-state
  flag (sibling of `senatePre17`): pre-12th-Amendment, many states choose
  presidential electors by **state legislature**, so the EV winner is decided by
  **who holds Gov/Sen/Rep** (majority party; Gov breaks ties), **not** by PV+dice.
  Phases out per-state by amendment/event; the "Nationwide Popular-Vote Surge" era
  event flips all-but-SC. Distinct from #44's `electionMethod`. `rep1800` §2-A.
- **Content-band era** *(architecture, `rep1800`)* — the design's actual notion of
  an "era": a fixed **band of available bills/events/draftees + a state-bias
  table**, entered/exited by **game-state + territory-ownership** triggers, NOT by
  calendar year. The clock runs ~30 yrs behind content (LA Purchase fires 1834).
  Contradicts the shipped `year % 4`/`year % 2` predicates. See gap-log #92.
- **Internal era names** *(era-sensitive, `rep1800`)* — the forum's eras are
  **finer-grained** than the 4-value `Era` enum: Republicanism (1800–20) →
  Democracy (1820–40) → Manifest Destiny (1840–56) → **Nationalism** (1856–68).
  The first three are **sub-bands of the shipped `nationalism` enum**;
  "Nationalism" internally = antebellum/Civil-War = the shipped `nationalism` value.
- **Cohens-v-Virginia precedent** *(early-republic, `rep1800`)* — an ahistorical
  scripted SCOTUS ruling that **federal law does NOT supersede existing state
  law**, making slavery a **state issue**: a slave state's slavery can be ended
  **only by a constitutional Amendment** (or a per-state Gov action). The engine
  substrate for the whole sectional design; there is **no mechanism to reverse an
  ahistorical ruling**. `rep1800` §2-B.
- **Command** — combat/leadership stat outside the 0–5 skill set; gates military
  command and kingmaker eligibility (`KINGMAKER_RULES.commandGateByScenario`).
- **Kingmaker / Protégé** — a high-Command mentor anoints a young protégé who
  graduates to higher office after ~20 years (`KINGMAKER_RULES`, types.ts:295).
- **Lingering phase (2.5.1)** — per-turn drift of national meters based on
  cabinet/conditions.
- **Sub-floor stats** — failed candidates / era figures in the dataset get
  deliberately weak electoral stats so they rarely win (CLAUDE.md dataset rules).
- **Lobby / Ideology / Interest cards** — the three faction card decks that
  define a faction's coalition and shift over time (types.ts:1298-1300).
- **Southern Unionist (trait) / Secessionists (pool)** *(1856-arc, `hd`)* — on
  secession, pols of seceded/border states go inactive into a "Secessionists"
  pool **unless** they hold the `Southern Unionist` trait; they return on the
  state's readmission. The draft dataset carries the trait on Southern pols.
- **Reconstruction +2-Red bias** *(1856-arc, `hd`)* — a time-boxed (8-yr,
  sunsetting) per-state partisan bias toward the incumbent party, granted by the
  Ironclad-Oath readmission plan; distinct from the permanent `State.bias`.
- **Acting President** *(1856-arc, `hd`)* — when the elected line fails (e.g. a
  foreign-born Speaker is ineligible), the Senate Pro Tempore acts; a **0-Command
  acting president is inert** (no exec actions, can't compel SCOTUS, can't be
  elected). The succession order is itself legislatable.
- **Primary Group (1–5)** *(Primary Era, `hd`)* — states opt into presidential
  primaries (via a Gov action) and are bucketed into 5 sequentially-voting groups;
  once any state opts in, the Primary Era begins (primaries precede conventions).
- **War Score** *(`hd`)* — per-theater Civil-War tally (+1 win / +3 Difficult land
  / −1 loss); **+10 auto-wins the theater**, else a carry-roll continues the war
  next half-term.

## Built vs. Designed — gap log

The heart of this doc; the roadmap is built from this. Rows are grouped by area.
Each is tagged `ingested` (forum-cited via a digest under
`docs/game/playtest-digests/`) or `codebase` (derived from the AMPU source
tree). Digest shorthands: **`gilded`** = the f4c7c2c4 1868 Gilded-Age digest;
**`fed`** = the f55d3e21 1788 federalism digest; **`1772s`** = the 85f8e6b4
1772 solo "aesthetic" digest; **`modern`** = the 3a9ac985 1948-campaign **2004→2020 successor** digest;
**`hd`** (= `house-divided`) = the 77db6e6f **1856-native** 1856→1904 digest
(cited `hd I-n` for its Part-I unique-system sections, else `hd POST n`);
**`hd1`** = the c015a0cb **"A House Divided" PART 1** digest (batch 16; the
**SEPARATE, EARLIER 1856-start run** distinct from `hd`/Part-2 — alt-history cast
**Chase president / Lincoln VP**, secession 1860-61 via a **bungled John-Brown's-
Raid decision**, **CSA president Herschel V. Johnson / Davis only War Secretary**,
Union wins 1864, ends the Era of Nationalism at 1868 then **restarts with vcczar's
revised Reconstruction rules**; the **first Civil-War→Reconstruction run played by
HUMANS on both sides of the Reconstruction tug-of-war**; cites `POST n`);
**`drums`** = the e1776bbd all-CPU 1841→1924 digest; **`pop`** = the c50d9da7

> **DEFECTS vs. GAPS.** This table is *missing features* (designed-but-unbuilt).
> Outright **bugs in shipped behavior** live in the separate "Confirmed shipped
> bugs" subsection below — the roadmap should treat those as fixes, not
> features.

### Platform / cross-cutting

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |

| 1 | **Multiplayer** | Single-player: one human faction (`isPlayer`), all others CPU (scenario1772.ts:64, scenario1856.ts:121) | **Multiplayer** — 8–10 human drafters across 2 parties (5 Blue + 5 Red), with handles; CPU factions only fill empty seats; **factions are transferable between humans mid-campaign** and CPU is a true per-faction fallback (`modern`: a new player took a CPU faction and won the presidency days later; `pop`: `Vee01` took R5 mid-thread, won the 2016 GOP nomination). (Both solo threads, `fed` + `1772s`, confirm the *same game* is also played solo-with-AI — so solo and multiplayer are two modes of one engine) | Multi-faction human control / turn arbitration; per-player handle + identity; async/seated turns; GM-style narration layer; CPU only as fallback; faction-handover support. (**7+ era confirmed** — very high confidence). **★ BUT the strongest design-intent statement (`nuke`) says the digital APP is 1-human-vs-9-CPU** (multiplayer "goes off the rails") even though the forum game is team MP — so the build is a **solo adaptation of a multiplayer game**; see #114. **`nuke` 1948 boot:** ~7–10 humans, **5 RED + 5 BLUE**, CPUs fill VACANT factions only (suffix `CPU`), humans rotate in/out. **`dem1820` 1820 boot:** 10 humans, **5 BLUE + 5 RED** (the cap holds an 8th era); **2 mid-thread handovers** (RingTheDink→Saucialiste; Euri CPU'd twice for absence) + CPU backfill — confirms faction transfer + per-faction CPU fallback | ingested (gilded 1, 12, 26, 113, 298; fed 1, 12; 1772s 1, 11; modern 1, 7, 424, 444; **hd 1, 38, 153, 456, 875**; **pop 1, 17, 24, 303, 312, 320; 1856-native + fresh-modern**; **nuke / POST 1, 16-17, 33, 483, 6966-6970; see #114**; **dem1820 POST 1, 412-414, 591, 601**; **terror2000 — CPU-heavy 2000-start: GA offered all-CPU / one-human-faction-each / 4-player setups (POST 1); started 8 humans + 2 CPU (RedCPU/BlueCPU), then BOTH CPU factions were handed to humans mid-thread (RedCPU→@ConservativeElector2, BlueCPU→@Pius XIII, POST 658-664) — CPU-as-per-faction-fallback + faction-handover, exactly the `oopscpu`/`nuke` pattern**; **modernday — 8 humans (4 Blue / 4 Red, NOT 5/5; the 5th-slot factions ran CPU all game: `ButtigiegCPU`/`HestiaCPU`/`BrunnellCPU`); GM CPU-substitutes inactive players "using CPU rules" (POST 55, 160, 852); mid-thread + era-boundary handovers (`pman` takes the Haley faction; the whole GM role itself handed Rodja→ebrk85; `Vicx`/`MrPotatoTed`/`ShortKing`/`pman` rotate in at the 2024 boundary, POST 1899-1910); CPU factions auto-accept the era-boundary faction-trade (POST 1949)**) |

| 232 | **★ STARTING-year draft needs a TIGHTER ideology restriction (2/faction) or manual seeding than a mid-game/rookie draft (3) — NEW (`primary2020`; distinct angle on #4/#171)** | The build has no draft-ideology restriction at all (#4 documents the early-era restriction as designed-only; #171 makes it an era-keyed toggle); neither captures the STARTING-draft-vs-mid-game-draft distinction | **A draft-balance finding from the May-2022 2022-start CPU draft (`primary2020` §5, POST 96, 99-104).** With 3 ideologies/faction at a COLD START the CPU produced incoherent factions: "Joe Biden is in charge of Bernie Sanders and AOC," only Seth Moulton could lead Harris/Warren, and Trump landed in a faction he wasn't even allowed to lead (couldn't be Party Leader; GM hand-traded him for Santorum). | 92 | **★ Eras-as-content-bands gated by game-state (NOT calendar year) — MULTI-SAVE CONFIRMED across 1772/1800/1820/1948; TWO-LEVEL model** | `Era` is a 4-value enum (`independence/federalism/nationalism/modern`, types.ts:1337); era predicates are pure calendar — `isDraftYear`/`isPresidentialYear` = `year % 4`, `isElectionYear` = `year % 2` (phases.ts:49–58); `shouldRunPhase` keys off the year | **THE headline architectural delta — now the most-corroborated finding in the KB.** An "era" is a **fixed band of available bills/events/draftees + a state-bias table**, advanced by half-term at a **game-state boundary**, NOT by calendar year — and **content is gated by TERRITORY OWNERSHIP**: bills/events/draftees for un-owned land are *invalid* (Indian Removal gated behind owning LA; Louisiana-born pols undraftable until LA owned). `rep1800`'s clock runs ~30 yrs behind its content (LA Purchase fires calendar 1834). **★ MULTI-SAVE CONFIRMED (batch 8):** the **1772-start `tea1772`** save and the **1800-start `rep1800`** save — two fully-independent campaigns begun **28 in-game years apart** — emit the **identical named era-bands at the same in-game dates** (Era of Federalists ~1800 → Age of Republicanism ~1820 → Era of Democracy ~1840 → Era of Manifest Destiny ~1856 → Era of Nationalism ~1868), each scored at its boundary. Transitions are game-state-gated, not annual (the CW band opens on an era event + DomStab/secession, not a date; Reconstruction ends piecemeal by legislation). The bands are **start-scenario-independent** (a 1772 start still closes Nationalism ~1868 on post-Reconstruction game-state). The forum's internal early eras (**Republicanism / Democracy / Manifest-Destiny**) are **sub-bands of the shipped `nationalism` enum**. **★ THIRD START CONFIRMED (batch 9, `nuke`):** the same engine runs in the MODERN half from a **1948 start**. **★ FOURTH START CONFIRMED (batch 10, `dem1820`):** a **1820 start** prints the identical per-faction draft-ideology bands — "**Era of Democracy (1820-1840)**" preceding "**Manifest Destiny (1840-1856)**" (the early sub-bands of `nationalism`) — so the model now holds across **1772 / 1800 / 1820 / 1948** starts. **★ TWO-LEVEL refinement (`nuke` settles a partial-digest conflict):** there are **two distinct mechanics**, an earlier extractor conflated them: **(a) point-banked Historical Eras** = the big content-bands (the original #92 mechanic): here **"Nuclear Age" = ONE era 1948–2000 → "Era of Terror" 2000–~2012**, entered at a **2000 point-banking boundary** with explicit "now that we are in the Era of Terror…" rule deltas; the *transition trigger* is the calendar year hitting 2000, but the *content/scoring/rules* are era-gated. **(b) decade/census boundaries WITHIN an era** (1972/1980/1990) = a SEPARATE schedule-fired mechanic doing THREE things at once: bulk **EV reallocation** state-by-state, **wholesale state-bias re-lean** (Blue5..Tossup..Red5), and **content rotation** (draft pool / lobby cards / era-activated industries). **★ CORRECTION — logged so it is not re-introduced: "Era of Neocons" / "Corporate Republicans" is a FACTION REBRAND (~1980–82) + a decade content-rotation label, NOT a point-banked band** (the shared sheet's tabs loosely name it, conflating decade-rotation with "era"; the digest is authoritative). | 114 | **★ Design intent: the APP is SOLO (1-human-vs-9-CPU); the forum game is team MP — the build is a solo adaptation; ★ the MANUAL CPU-faction burden is the load-bearing cost (2 1772 runs DIED of it)** — NEW | Build IS already single-player (one `isPlayer` faction, 9 CPU) — this row VALIDATES the shipped shape against design intent (most other rows are MP-vs-solo deltas) | **The strongest corpus statement of the digital app's intended mode.** The designer states the computer game is built for **1 human vs 9 CPU** because human multiplayer "goes off the rails"; the points system is for CPUs + enthusiasm, not humans (low points = better draft order, so humans could tank it). The tabletop/forum game is team MP with CPU backfill — **both are true**, the app is the solo adaptation. **★ Roadmap consequence:** this **VALIDATES the shipped single-player shape and the solo-first / multiplayer-last sequencing** — but means the **CPU-faction AI is the load-bearing system the app needs** (entirely unexercised by this ~7–10-human playtest), and a large apparatus that humans drove in the forum (party-leader elections, conversions, kingmaker pairings, committee assignment, cross-faction endorsements, forced 3rd-party runs, convention behavior) **must be AI-driven in the solo build** (ties to the CPU-AI cluster #70-#78 + DH-8). ### Legislative (committees, bills, crises, budget)

| 8 | **Committee block-and-replace + chair-blocks-one + repeating-bill auto-block** | Bills proposed → committee → floor (phases 2.6.1–2.6.3). No block-and-replace | Committee chair can **block and/or replace** a bill from their own committee's domain (Block alone kills it); some bills can't be blocked. Chair eligibility requires prior committee service (`modern`: **Leadership OR Legis ≥ 2**). Bills marked with a star/`##` are block-eligible. **`pop` confirms a clean chair-blocks-ONE rule** (POST 487-490): chair may BLOCK exactly **one proposal** from the slate **before** the vote, then the committee votes on the rest. Also: **repeating-bill committee auto-block** — if the same legislation is proposed twice in the same cycle, the Chairman auto-blocks the duplicate (`pop` POST 712-714) | Add committee-chair "block-and-replace" action with same-committee replacement check + chair-eligibility gate + **chair-blocks-exactly-one-pre-vote** + duplicate-bill auto-block. (**6+ era confirmed**; pervasive — `hd` sharpens the rule: a chair may replace only a bill whose **proposer has LESS Legislative AND lacks Efficient**; `pop` confirms in fresh-modern boot) | ingested (gilded 160-163; fed 160, 209, 305, 380, 563, 723; modern 46, 285, 1312, 1870; **hd 195-203, 469, 5123**; **pop 487-490, 712-714**) |
| 9 | **Bill packaging / bundling** | Each bill votes separately | Chair can package multiple committee bills into one floor vote that passes/fails as one; **packages can't be split-voted** (`modern` 1341). Federalism nuance: a chair **won't bundle** a net-negative bill *unless* it's a statehood bill; CPU bundles ~75%. Used as a weapon (`modern`: pair a poison-pill with a desired bill so both die). **`pop` reconfirms** in a fresh-modern boot: after committee votes, chair **packages passing bills together OR leaves them separate** (POST 502-507) — load-bearing weaponization, **4 unrelated GOP bills jammed into Bill #3** to amortize sign/veto cost (POST 507, 542) | Add packaging + vote aggregation; bundling-eligibility rule; no-split-vote constraint. | 230 | **★ Competitive-map / swing-state set — cap which states can flip so the jitter can't swing safe states — NEW (`primary2020`; election scoring)** | `calcStateVote` (`phaseRunners.ts:3685-3723`) scores EVERY state identically and lets the `(Math.random()-0.5)*8` jitter flip anything; no swing-state set / safe-state floor | **A NEW election-scoring constraint surfaced in the May-2022 stress-test (`primary2020` §3, POST 28, 40-50).** The 2020-map re-rolls repeatedly produced implausible flips — Dem wins OK/KS/AK; "Florida votes to the right of Mississippi"; "Wyoming and Kentucky highly competitive"; CA/NV margins swapped. Root cause (POST 28): the state-bias MARGIN BONUS only fires above a sub-point CUTOFF (≥6, debated ≥4), so safe states never LOCK and tiny rolls flip them. V deferred ("might wait until we can do elections on CPU… run 100+ tests a day," POST 61). | 45 | **Generic war system (any war, any era)** | `revolutionaryWar.ts` is 1772-scoped | A generic war phase used in every era (War of 1795, Barbary, 1812; `modern` Grenada). Per half-term 1–N battles (`modern`: **naval then land, ≥1 naval win required first**), each with **Chance of Success = base + commander-mil(×10) + (SecDef+JointChiefs ×2) + difficulty + mil-prep(+25) + benchmarks**, d100; **War Score** accumulates (win +1, lose −3); a separate **war-end roll** (`warscore × ~×2 multiplier → %` to lose outright); **Momentum** = turn-vs-turn; defeated commander gains Incompetent + relieved → confirmation/back-fill cascade; loss applies a debuff package (Party Pref −3, **permanent −1 election malus** for the pres). **`drums` reconfirms battle formula across maps 5/8/10/11 + WWI + Mexico** — identical structure (Difficulty + Planning(SecMil+CoS) + Officer×10 + MilPrep + Benchmarks → win%); **auto-win at WS ≥ +11** (POST 5111, 6708); **post-war defeat % = `|WS|×2×10`**; **officer KIA on natural 1** (auto-nominated replacement, unanimous confirm); **catastrophic 100/100**: -3 WS + general loses 1 Mil + Leadership + Military Leader (POST 2728) | Generalize to a `War` model: success-chance formula, naval→land phasing, warscore/momentum/end-multiplier, officer-promotion/Incompetent + confirmation cascade, loss-debuff, **WS≥+11 auto-win, |WS|×2×10 post-war defeat, KIA-on-nat-1, catastrophic 100/100 cascade**, **+ CONCURRENT MULTI-WAR support: several wars run in the same half-term** (`new1772`: Revolutionary War + a parallel Invasion-of-Canada track simultaneously; `tea1772`: Mexican-American Phase 1/2 + Apache Rounds 1–4 + Navajo Phases 1–2 all concurrent). NEW SUB-DESIGN — **naval as a DIFFICULTY MODIFIER, not a standalone win-condition**: fight ≥1 naval + ≥1 ground per phase, naval FIRST; a naval WIN gives the next land general +1 Mil (75%) for that battle only, a naval LOSS −1 Mil — so naval persists and FEEDS land difficulty rather than "ending forever" (the design fix for the shipped DH-79 bug). Open: the French-alliance auto-win (`revolutionaryWar.ts:259`) does NOT generalize — vcczar (POST 25) calls it historically UNIQUE as a war-WINNER; other alliances can LOSE you a war (CSA + UK/France), so "alliance = auto-win" must not be a generic rule. ★ GM ROADMAP PRIORITY: vcczar rules war is "a side show for AMPU"; the War-Score redesign is explicitly **deferred to POST-LAUNCH** (POST 26) — desired, not a pre-launch must-have. | 39 | **Constitutional Amendments as durable, separately-ratified state — MUTATE CORE RULES** | `constitutionalConvention.ts` covers the *initial* Constitution; later amendments not surveyed | Amendments pass Congress then go **to the states for ratification**. They durably change rules: term-length, popular-vote-everywhere, VP-vacancy fill, court size, suffrage. **Ratification mechanism + threshold vary by era** (fed/gilded by legislatures, often unanimous / "2/3 of states"; **`modern` by GOVERNORS, 40 of 53**; **`rep1800` by Govs at 2/3, lowered from 3/4 by an earlier amendment, taking effect the next half-term, with Puritan/Integrity Gov overrides**), and amendments need a **2/3-House supermajority** (382/572). A **grandfather clause** can exempt the sitting officeholder. **★ `rep1800` makes the rule-mutation concrete — amendments rewrite the constitutional shape MID-GAME**: the **"Sexenio" experiment** ratified 3 amendments in 1834 that turned the Presidency into a Mexico-style **single 6-year term** (16th = Universal White Male Suffrage; 17th = One-Term Limit; 18th = Six-Year Term), with a 25th-style succession rule (a VP elevated past the half-way point can't run); terms later reverted by amendment. **No grandfather clause modeled** (the real 22nd exempts the incumbent; GM: "my rules" — design hole). | 100 | **SCOTUS can OVERTURN a ratified Amendment (review/repeal loop) + threshold-itself-amendable** — NEW | Amendments treated as durable (#39); no judicial-review-of-amendment path; no mutable amendment threshold | **★ A ratified constitutional Amendment is NOT final — SCOTUS can strike it.** Via a **Governor-requested judicial review**, the Court can **overturn a ratified Amendment** (`tea1772`: the timeline's 13th "White-Male Suffrage" Amendment was overturned **4–3**, reverting it to a mere governor-action that Congress may re-pass; a Taylor-McDowell law was similarly overturned). | 160 | **★ The Great Depression is a SCRIPTED ERA EVENT with VARIABLE timing that carries a BUNDLE of meter shocks + an EconStab CASCADE — and the era's static party-modifiers are decoupled from it (balance) — NEW (`ideo1928`)** | No EconStab/economic-stability meter, no Great-Depression event, no `progressive` era in shipped code (`src/types.ts` `Era` = `independence/federalism/nationalism/modern`; `Meter.tsx` is a generic UI shell; 0 hits for `econStab`/`depression` in `src/`) | **The headline 1928 finding + the concrete face of the EconStab meter (#116, interwar angle).** The crash is **NOT auto-fired on the real Oct-1929 schedule** — the in-game economy stayed "great" into Jan 1930 (`ideo1928` POST 567) and players debated keeping prior-era modifiers **"until the great depression event hits, if it ever does"** (POST 545); it finally fired in the 1930-1932 turn (POST 862). The **"Wall Street Crash and Great Depression" event is a META-EVENT** carrying a bundle: **EconStab −4 (→Recession & Crisis), Rev/Budget −2 (→overspending/Crisis), QoL −1, Mil Prep −1, Party-Pref −3** + a binary presidential choice (let-markets-resolve / congressional-bailout). The event text encodes the **interconnected-global-economy** ("The London Stock Exchange crash has led to our own crash on Wall Street"). **EconStab CASCADE:** at Recession, **2 random industries drop −1 nationwide in EVERY state** + a Dom-Stab-drop chance; industry-leadership flips → **EV changes** (CO+1/OK−1 here, POST 866-887); EconStab also **gates Dom-Stab/QoL increases** while in crisis (POST 723). **★ BALANCE DELTA (GA post-mortem, POST ch18-8): "These era bonuses are SUPER STRONG… the 'Depression' wasn't nearly as bad this time around. That's what caused a LOT of the reaction against Hoover historically"** — the era's BLUE-favorable party modifiers are **baked statically into the era band, decoupled from the crash event**, so the GOP craters even when the economy is healthy (POST 446/545); AND the modeled severity was too weak (climbed out of crisis in ~4 yrs via ordinary legislation + gov "lower taxes" actions, POST 1601, 1046). **Crisis-gated bills:** "Allow the Federal Reserve to generate currency during economic crises" is INELIGIBLE until the economy hits panic/crisis (POST 337) → becomes legal only after the crash (POST 1040). | Build the crash-as-scripted-event: an `economicStability` meter + a Great-Depression META-event that applies the multi-meter shock bundle + the EconStab cascade (2-random-industries −1 nationwide → EV reflow; meter-gating of other meters in crisis); **event-gate the era's party-modifier bias to the Depression firing** (not static) AND give the crash a persistent drag ordinary bills can't instantly undo (human call); crisis-gated legislation eligibility keyed to the EconStab level. The prior threads saw meters/enthusiasm/SCOTUS in pieces; the `modern` thread
supplies the concrete, mature specifications below — the spine of the modern
election engine.

| 50 | **The named meter bank (concrete set) + crisis/cascade rules** | `NationalMeters` exists (types.ts:1399): revenue, economic, military, domestic, honest, quality, planet | The concrete modern bank, each on a **banded-text ladder** nudged ±1 by phases/cabinet/"Lingering"/"Revision to Mean"/"Volatility"/legislation: **Revenue-Budget, Economic Stability, Military Preparedness, Domestic Stability, Honest Gov't, Quality of Life, Planet's Health, Party Preference** + **per-ideology enthusiasm** + the **8 per-power relation meters**. | 51 | **Faction-enthusiasm / Party-Preference election engine** | `Enthusiasm` (ideology×party −5..+5) + `partyPreference` exist; the driving algorithm is not in code | Every ideology holds an **enthusiasm position on a Blue↔Red track**; **Party Preference** is the master partisan meter. After legislation scoring a fixed **4-part rule** reshuffles enthusiasm by which faction gained most/least for the dominant vs opposition party. A running **faction Score** drives this and pays **end-of-era awards**; a team's **lowest-scoring faction penalizes teammates**. "State of the Meters" then maps the whole bank → per-election bonuses (#18). **`drums` independently confirms the 4-step loop across a 3rd era** (POSTS 50, 86, 295, 442, 2537, 2726, 2879, 3115) — (1) events award/penalize per-faction; (2) **most-points dominant faction shifts +1**; (3) **least-points dominant faction shifts -1**; (4) **most-points opposition +1 / least-points opposition -1**; per-faction enthusiasm shifts: dominant ±1, others ±1 per faction-level comparison. **Era-end scoring rewards** (POST 4477): +5 most points, +3 second, etc. **±3 cap on per-phase ideology swings** (POST 4574) — Tyler patched mid-thread; Mods swung +7 raw → capped at +3. **Cabinet enthusiasm-via-lobbies overwhelms presidential signal** without cap (POSTS 877, 880). **`pop` reconfirms in a fresh-modern boot:** per-ideology enthusiasm ±/Party Pref ticks every phase (debate +1, scandal -1, convention strong-ticket +1, October Surprise +1, Planet Health crisis -2 multi-ideology); confirms the same 14-dim per-ideology engine drives the modern arc | Implement the 4-part enthusiasm-reshuffle algorithm + faction Score economy + era-end awards + lowest-faction penalty + **±3 per-phase ideology-swing cap**; wire to the meter→election map. (**5-era cpu-confirmed; ★ FORK-RESOLVED**) | ingested (modern 96, 134, 722, 768, 945, 1080, 2039; **hd 1394, 1568, 6535, 7799, I-12**; **drums 50, 86, 295, 442, 877, 880, 647, 813, 979, 1880, 2537, 2726, 2879, 3044-3065, 3115, 4477, 4574**; **pop 53, 212, 220, 223, 232, 234, 242, 463, 543, 567, 972**; **arkzag — ★ SETTLES the `dem1820` #18/#51 fork: the final chunk publishes the 4-step rule VERBATIM and it MATCHES `drums` (not Ted's "every state" nor Matt's "primaries only"): per Congress's by-card→by-faction legislation tally — (1) faction with MOST pts for dominant party → cards +1 enth toward dominant; (2) LEAST pts for dominant → −1 away; (3) MOST pts for opposition → +1 toward DOMINANT ("taking care of their needs"), only if it gains pts; (4) LEAST pts from opposition → +2 toward OPPOSITION ("furious at incumbent"), even if it gains pts — shifts STACK; paired w/ a meter-overflow ±cap. opposition-faction "+1 toward dominant only if it gains pts / merely-losing-least does NOT qualify" rule reconfirmed, POST 446-447**; **modernday (current-rules) — the running faction-Score economy + era-end awards exercised live (banked totals at the 2024 boundary, #68/POST 1871) then RESET to 0; conversion %s: party-leader-only flips opposing-party Pliable 10%/Moderate 5% (+5% Propagandist); faction-leader flips same-party Pliable+same-ideology 33%/10% [POST 1966]**; **pop2012b — 2nd 2012-start corroboration: per-ideology enthusiasm + Party Pref tick every phase (debate +1 / scandal −1 / strong-ticket +1 / Oct-Surprise −1 / Lingering-crisis −1) and the faction-Score economy awards/penalizes on EVERY confirmation/election/event/SCOTUS-phase/signed-bill (+5000 general winner; +400 SCOTUS confirm; ±100-300/bill); the "PRE-MIDTERMS STATE OF METERS" prints the 2-layer map verbatim, see #18 — POST 285, 584, 632, 840, ch11**; **★★ CARD-ASSIGNMENT ALGORITHM — CANONICAL (batch 31, `rulebook` §I POST 10, the most data-dense post; the authoritative source spec for the #50/#51 card LAYER under the enthusiasm engine): each faction holds Ideology + Interest + Lobby cards re-evaluated EVERY 2 YEARS, scoring +/- points when relevant laws/events occur, driven by the STRENGTHS of the faction's own politicians. ◆ Ideology cards (6: Progressive/Liberal/Moderate/Conservative/Traditionalist/Populist [= most LW+RW Populists combined]) → the faction with the MOST pols of that ideology (PLURALITY wins, e.g. 40 Lib/39 Mod/38 Con ⇒ Liberal); ties → cards SHARED; a faction may hold >1; EVERY faction MUST have ≥1 ideology card — if none, it gets its party's Historical-Era ideology (era-specific). ◆ Interest cards (8: Nationalist/Expansionist/RW-Activist/LW-Activist/Reformist/Civil-Rights/Pacifist/Theocrat) → most-pols-with-that-interest; Theocrat ✗ Progressive. ◆ Lobby cards (25+, each keyed to an EXPERTISE) → most-matching-expertise-pols; full ban table (Wall Street[Econ] ✗ Prog/Pop/Reformist; Big Oil&Gas ✗ Prog/Lib/LW-Activist; LW-Media MUST have Lib/Prog; RW-Media MUST have Con/Trad; Military-Industrial ✗ Prog/Pacifist; Big Ag/Transportation join anyone). ◆ 5-POLITICIAN FLOOR: interest AND lobby cards each require the faction to have ≥5 pols with the required interest/expertise; if no faction qualifies, NO ONE gets that card. ◆ CASCADE: when a faction is INELIGIBLE for a card, it cascades to the next-most-relevant ELIGIBLE faction. This plurality + compatibility/ban tables + 5-pol-floor + cascade is the canonical card-assignment engine the shipped meters/enthusiasm partial implementation lacks; it is the LAYER under #50/#51 and the FL ideology-binding (which enthusiasm meter the faction scores on). ### Antebellum / Civil-War / Reconstruction systems (`hd` + `rep1800`)

The `house-divided` thread is the **first 1856-native procedural record** of the
antebellum → Civil-War → Reconstruction → Progressive-finale machinery. **`rep1800`
now corroborates these rows from a SECOND, DISTINCT campaign with DIVERGENT
outcomes** (a different Civil War: fires ~1846 off DomStab=1 not a secession
convention; the President defects to lead the CSA; UK-intervention theater; a
guerrilla 4th stage; National Republicans not Whigs) — strong independent
confirmation that the engine is one ruleset, plus new variant content. The shipped
`scenario1856.ts` / `eraEvents1856.ts` spine **ends at the Trent Affair (1861)** and
has none of this — the war these campaigns play is host-improvised content.

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |

### CPU AI specifications (NEW — `drums`-derived, **`oopscpu`-corroborated**; resolves DH-8 heuristics)

The `drums` all-CPU playtest is the **first explicit forum record of CPU
heuristics**. The shipped game is single-player; **every faction except the
player is CPU**, so these rows are first-class build requirements. They
**RESOLVE the bulk of DH-8** (CPU AI under-spec); the REMAINING DH-8 gaps live
in DH-19..DH-22 below. **★ Batch 13 (`oopscpu`) is the second all-CPU run and
the first DELIBERATE CPU-ruleset interrogation** (Ted-run, explicitly "to find
where the rules are insufficient" — POST 1, 5). It **corroborates #70/#72/#73/
#74/#75/#76 from a founding-era angle**, adds **NEW CPU sub-gaps OC-1..OC-8**
below, and pins several **Ted rulings** (the post-election Command-loss rule, the
pre-12A CPU nomination trio, the help-allies gov-term sub-rule). **Coverage
caveat: the convention CPU AI (#71) is UNTESTED by `oopscpu`** because the 1788
pre-12A era runs no conventions — leadership IRV (#70) is the only convention
proxy here. **Shipped reality:** the engine has CPU code for the meta-passes
(draft pick / career track / relocation / ideology shift / conversion — see
`phaseRunners.ts` `RELOCATION_ODDS.cpuGate`, `IDEOLOGY_SHIFT_ODDS.cpu`) but
**none of the #70–#78 handler suite** — those remain designed-only.

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 70 | **CPU leadership / Speaker / PPT IRV bloc-vote + 3-inconclusive-ballot collective endorse** | Leadership phase exists; no CPU bloc-vote model | Authoritative IRV tie-break ladder confirmed across **4+ maps** (Speaker, PPT, Sen Maj/Min Leader/Whip, House Maj/Min Leader/Whip elections): (1) ballot 1, each faction casts as a UNIT for own/closest candidate; (2) **closest ideology**; (3) **highest PV**; (4) **highest Legislative skill**; (5) random same-party as last resort. **After 3 inconclusive ballots, CPUs collectively endorse a winner** (confirmed POSTS 5272, 5841, 6099). Designer patches: **continuous IRV elimination** (no ballot-3 random collapse, POST 3419) + **randomize only on FIRST elimination** (POST 3419). **No reciprocity / vote-trading exists** (POST 4875 — designer comment "the CPUs don't understand reciprocity"). Closest-ideology can flip leadership to the minority party (POST 3419, Magoffin/Cons-Dem 1880). Asymmetric on-win bundle (#28) | Implement the 5-step IRV ladder + bloc-vote unit per faction + continuous elimination + first-round-only randomization + 3-inconclusive-ballot collective endorse + asymmetric on-win bundle. Human factions do NOT auto-collapse — must manually endorse. **No-reciprocity is architectural** — DH-20 below. | 208 | **★ CPU LEGISLATIVE/CONFIRMATION logic is UNSPECIFIED — filibuster-override, majority/minority-leader vote rule, and cross-party cabinet caps were all GM-improvised at modern scale — NEW (`welcome2future`, `GM⇒App`)** | The #70-#78 cluster + OC-1..OC-8 cover CPU candidate-selection / draft / crisis-vote / vacancy-fill, but **none specify how a CPU runs the LEGISLATIVE + CONFIRMATION machinery**: how a CPU Majority Leader decides to override (or not) a filibuster, how the maj/min leaders themselves VOTE, or the cross-party cabinet limits | **The clearest mass-CPU legislative-behavior sample in the corpus (8 of 10 factions on CPU rules at modern scale) — and it exposes that large swaths of CPU legislative behavior are undefined and were invented on the fly.** `welcome2future` ran a full modern turn hands-off without stalling, but the GM had to improvise: **(a)** *"there is NO rule for whether a CPU Majority Leader overrides a filibuster"* → improvised "won't override own party unless it targets his faction" (posts 331, 343 — CPU senators with the right profile DID filibuster nominees: Mike Lee killed Sullivan+Locke, Cruz killed Solis, filibustered pols gained `Controversial`); **(b)** no rule for **how maj/min leaders themselves vote** → invented "support own party + within-2-ideology-clicks; iron-fist → within-1" (post 322); **(c)** **cross-party cabinet caps** felt "too easy" ("weird that it's so Republican") → GM rewrote them mid-thread (≤25% accept w/o integrity; ≤1 cross-party in top-4; ≤3 total; ≤1 ideology step away, posts 307-349). All three are `GM⇒App` automation requirements at the heart of the "subsume the GM" charter. Pairs with #52/#172 (confirmation thresholds + Nuclear-Option), #25 (cabinet), the #70-#78 CPU cluster, DH-76 (the no-cloture/no-override rule gap) | Formalize CPU legislative/confirmation rules as deterministic engine logic: (a) CPU filibuster-override decision for a maj leader (own-party-unless-targets-my-faction baseline); (b) maj/min-leader own vote rule (own-party + within-2-ideology-clicks, iron-fist within-1); (c) cross-party cabinet caps (≤1 in top-4, ≤3 total, ≤1 ideology step, integrity gate). Pairs with #52/#172/#25/DH-76 + the #70-#78 cluster | ingested (**welcome2future posts 307-349, 322, 331, 343; the hands-off modern run is ALSO the most complete modern CPU-turn spec in the corpus — see the #114/#110 annotations**; **★★ batch 35 EXTENDS — `redbutton1960` (3c3c46f0) hands us TWO GM-improvised CPU subsystems verbatim (`GM⇒App`; POST 11 "Can't wait for the actual game so the computer can take over a lot of the tedious processes"): (1) ★ CPU moderate-faction SWING-VOTE model — *"the moderate faction starts at 50-50 but the bill gains or loses support based on (1) which party proposed the bill, (2) if their party leader supports it or not, and (3) the actual make-up of the faction"* — applied ONLY to MODERATE factions because partisan factions' votes are obvious ("easy when the bill helps or hurts your faction"); a base-rate-plus-modifiers form COMPLEMENTARY to `welcome2future`'s leader-level own-vote rule. The build's CPU legislative engine should subsume BOTH (a faction-level swing model AND a leader-level vote rule). (2) ★ Presidential PRESSURE (Command-driven) — see #182: roll (Command) d6 → a 5-6 rerolls → result ×10 = % of a faction swayed. ⚠ RECONCILE: this Presidential-pressure variant uses COMMAND (this thread) vs the `rulebook` §Y/§M2 "President may convert up to (Legislative#) senators on a 5-6" which uses LEGISLATIVE — two designer-improvised forms; tech-lead to pick the canonical stat. Also DH-53/legislation-scoring corroborated here: the Farm-Subsidy bill = +100 pts to every ag-state Gov/Sen/Rep (a geographic bill→points table). redbutton1960 POST 11, 17-18**) |

### NEW mechanics surfaced by `pop` (fresh-modern-boot deltas)

The `pop` thread is the **first record of how a modern-era scenario BOOTS from
cold** (vs. `modern`'s 60-yr continuation from a 1948 campaign). It surfaces a
small cluster of HIGH-signal mechanics around the **scenario-boot model** + the
**Era-of-Populism mechanical surface** that the modern-era flat card pool
configures rather than introduces. These are net-new rows; the bulk of `pop`
**corroborates** §22 systems already in the gap log (see #1, #8, #9, #10, #12,
#47, #50, #51, #52, #67 strengthened above).

| 188 | **★ "Big red button" nuclear-war LOSS condition is premise-only — undocumented as a mechanic and never fired** — NEW (`redbutton`; corroborates #88/#106) | `EraEvent.triggersGameEnd` exists (types.ts:1635); no nuclear/MAD subsystem (#106); no meter-floor nuclear path | The 1960 "Big Red Button" run is **named and framed around a literal nuclear-war loss** — GM, POST 1: *"no one wins if that big red button gets hit"* — presented as the campaign's defining stake alongside Vietnam, the Space Race, and domestic turmoil. **But it is entirely undocumented as a mechanic and NEVER FIRED:** the run paused at the **1962-64 scripted block (~in-game 1962-63)**, before any Cuban-Missile-Crisis analog could escalate. The only Cold-War "nuclear" content that *did* appear is **event/legislation-flavor on the generic engine** — a **sign/don't-sign Nuclear Test Ban Treaty** scripted event (President Bricker signs it; relation/meter rolls follow, POST 1677-1688), a "treat Cuba as a client state" **bill**, and **Bay of Pigs** as a legislative/minority-flip lever (chunk-016 POST 1148). So how a nuclear-war end-state would trigger (meter floor? scripted escalation chain? war-engine?) is **unknown** — confirming #88 (dramatic end-conditions exist as designer *intent*, not built systems) and #106 (no purpose-built nuclear/MAD subsystem) | Negative-scope datum for the roadmap: the headline "nuclear-war loss" of a 1960 scenario is **unbuilt and unspecified**. ### Early-republic systems (NEW — `rep1800`-only; the 1800–1856 gap-fill)

The `rep1800` thread is the **first procedural record of the 1800–1856 early
republic** (Jeffersonian → Era-of-Good-Feelings → Jacksonian → Manifest-Destiny).
The rows below have no shipped representation and were not surfaced by the prior
seven threads. The headline architecture finding lives in #92 (cross-cutting);
these are the era-content + subsystem deltas. Several **refine** existing rows
(noted) rather than duplicate — dedup is hard here.

| # | Area | In the build today | In the documented design | Delta / requirement | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 93 | **12th-Amendment before/after state machine (conventions + VP-on-ticket are unlocked, not always-on)** | No 12th-Amendment toggle; conventions (phase 2.9.2) + VP exist unconditionally; no `electorsByLegislature` flag | A genuine **era-specific state machine** absent from all post-12A threads. **PRE-12A:** **no conventions at all**; many states pick presidential electors **by legislature** — for those the EV winner = **who holds Gov/Sen/Rep** (majority party; Gov breaks ties), **NOT** PV+dice (a per-state `electorsByLegislature` flag, sibling of `senatePre17`; in 1804 CT/GA/MA/NJ/NY/SC/VT were legislature-decided). **Passing the in-game "President Elections by Party Tickets Amendment" (= the 12A)** is the single toggle that **unlocks conventions + the separate VP-on-the-ticket** rule (and gates "Separate VP Election" + "Send VP to Shore Up Support", confirming #91). The **"Nationwide Popular-Vote Surge" era event** later flips **all states except SC** off legislature-electors — the end-state of the machine. Also the **first fully-recorded FIRST convention** (resolves `gilded` open-Q #10) | Add the 12A as a **toggleable amendment state** that gates conventions + VP-on-ticket; add a per-state `electorsByLegislature` flag flipped off by amendment/the popular-vote-surge event; pre-12A EC = state-control tally not PV+dice. the eventual computerized AMPU. Its thesis: *a political sim wearing
fantasy-sports / trading-card clothes with an old-school almanac vibe.* None of
this is a deliberate visual language in the shipped UI (functional pages only).

| 145 | **★ Debt-table meter effect = roll CATEGORY then bonus/penalty, ONE meter only — RULED** — NEW | Lingering debt step may apply effects to multiple meters | **Ted-agreed (`oopscpu` POST 148-153):** a debt level rolls FIRST for which meter category it may hit, THEN rolls whether it hits — it can move **only one meter**, not all of them; N/A categories are skipped (just roll the Rev/Budget effect). (Umbrella had hit both DomStab AND HonestGov; corrected to one.) | Make the Lingering/credit-debt effect a two-step single-meter roll. Refines #67 (Lingering bank) / #88 (debt). | ingested (**oopscpu POST 148-153**) |
| 146 | **★ Procedural rulings: new offices staffed next-2.3; appointment-replacement no point-loss; 9th/10th draft bonus = first-PICK — RULED** — NEW | Office-staffing timing / appointment-replacement scoring / draft-bonus scope under-specified | Three small `oopscpu` Ted rulings: **(a)** a bill that CREATES an office (AG, Bank President) staffs it at the **next 2.3 appointments phase**, not immediately (POST 89); **(b)** an incumbent **replaced by appointment loses NO points** — being replaced at an appointed post isn't a "loss" (POST 105-108); **(c)** the 9th/10th-place **draft skill bonus** applies to the faction's **first pol actually drafted**, not its first-ROUND pick (so a failed first-round attempt doesn't waste it) (POST 239). | Wire office-creation→next-appointments-phase staffing; suppress point-loss on appointment-replacement; apply the 9th/10th draft bonus to the first successful pick. | ingested (**oopscpu POST 89, 105-108, 239**) |
| 147 | **Tariff as a national integer %-rate set by a literal rate-bill (+ mutually-exclusive currency regimes)** — NEW | Tariff is only a meter-nudging flavor bill (#3); no national rate state; no `MonetaryRegime` | **★ The tariff is voted as a literal national percentage.** `gild1868` floors competing rate-bills — "**Set average tariff rate to 36%**" vs "**Set average tariff rate to 25% and standardize and reform the tariff system**" (POST 6240; ch67/76/77 roll-calls) — i.e. legislation sets a single national integer the parties fight over (protectionist GOP high vs reform low). Currency is a parallel mutually-exclusive regime: a **Gold-Standard Act** (removes greenbacks, deflationary) vs **Bimetallism/Free-Silver** vs a **National Banking System** (paper currency + war bonds). **BUG/relationship gap:** `gild1868` had **Bimetallism AND the Gold Standard Act both active at once despite being mutually exclusive** (POST 6245) — no exclusivity constraint between currency-regime bills | Add a `tariffRate` national integer set/changed by a `Set Average Tariff Rate to N%` bill type (+ standardize/reform variant); add a `MonetaryRegime` enum (Gold / Bimetallic / Free-Silver / National-Bank) where the regime bills are **mutually exclusive** (passing one deactivates the others — the missing relationship constraint). Sharpens #3; pairs with #42 bill-relationship graph | ingested (**gild1868 1, 836, 884, 6240, 6245**; ch67/76/77 tariff roll-calls) |
| 148 | **20-year auto-expiring Reconstruction regime + appointment-by-leadership + Solid-South bias sunset** — NEW | No Reconstruction subsystem (#57 is the readmission/war-victory spec); no auto-expiry timer; no appointment-by-Speaker/PPT | **★ `gild1868` (native 1868) models Reconstruction as a time-boxed regime, not just a war-victory state (#57):** it **auto-ends 20 years from initiation** (1864 → **1884**, explicitly "to prevent a one-party state," POST 73/76); while active, seceded-state Gov/Sen/Rep seats are **APPOINTED, not elected** — military Govs Pres-appointed but **must be the majority-Congress party**, **Senators chosen by the faction controlling the Pres Pro Tempore**, **Reps by the faction controlling the Speaker**, appointees **cannot have seceded** (rules 3.0.32/3.0.35, POST 70/143/330); GOP gets **+2 in those appointments/elections**; at expiry the +2 bias **sunsets and southern states flip to a Blue-heavy Solid South** (FL/GA/LA Blue+3→Blue+5, VA Blue+2→Blue+5, POST 5145). (4) **seat LOSS** — existing districts re-roll: 50% no change / 25% tossup / 25% → the party with the FEWEST growth lobbies (shrinking states trend nostalgic/conservative; growing states trend liberal). | 250 | **★ House-seat-COMPETITION model fork — how multiple focus-Rep seats in one state compete (per-seat vs free-for-all top-N vs single multi-member pool) + the CPU-keeps-incumbents-in-seat rule + seat-lock-released-on-reapportionment — NEW (`electiondisc`; Decision-gated likely; sharpens #219/#55/#191)** | Shipped focus-Reps are flat per-state `representativeIds: string[]` (`types.ts:1327`) with NO seat-competition grouping, NO per-seat race structure, and NO reapportionment-driven seat-lock logic — distinct from #219 (how seats are SIZED) and #191 (per-seat partisan LEAN); this row is the COMPETITION STRUCTURE | **The design-origin discussion (Apr 2022, MrPotatoTed-led) of how a state's multiple focus-Rep seats compete; raised + informally dispositioned but NOT ratified by vcczar — an OPEN design fork.** Under focus-Reps a state with multiple seats runs them as separate independent races (GA-1 vs GA-2); seats are NOT geographic districts ("Bill Clinton AR-1, Hillary AR-2 despite the same house"; relocation modeled via the pol's alternate-states, POST 5/8/15/16). THREE options on the table: **(A) per-seat (status quo)** — separate race per seat, candidate picks GA-1 *or* GA-2, per-seat primaries (**informally PREFERRED/kept** — "GA-1 stays in GA-1's lane," Ted POST 5; not ratified); **(B) free-for-all** — one pool, no per-seat primaries, top-2 overall take GA's 2 seats (raised, not adopted); **(C) single multi-member pool** — every GA candidate competes in ALL GA races at once (OrangeP47 POST 13 says this is what Ted's explanation logically implied but "I don't know how to make that work"). The motivating quirk (POST 1/2): under A, both incumbents can run against each other for GA-1, leaving GA-2 to outsiders → **CPU RULE (NEW concrete requirement): CPU keeps incumbents in their current seat by default; a HUMAN may override** ("that's the human's fault," Ted POST 2). Rezi's alt (POST 3): a hard seat-LOCK releasing **only when state rep count changes** (reapportionment) so the pol gets a chance to move — sharpens #55's seat-locked incumbency with the unlock trigger; reapportionment edge (POST 5): if GA shrinks to 1 Rep, the displaced GA-2 incumbent becomes eligible to contest GA-1 (so seat count must be dynamic per era and the eligibility shuffle keys off it). If A: implement per-seat race grouping + per-seat primaries; **CPU rule = incumbents run in their current seat, humans may override**; seat-lock released on reapportionment (dynamic per-era seat count); the reapportionment eligibility shuffle (state→fewer-seats frees the displaced incumbent). Likely a setup/Decision-gated choice. | 199 | **Confirmation-rejection trait cascade (rejected nominee → Controversial, then Incompetent; blocks re-nomination)** — NEW | No automatic trait cascade on a rejected appointment; #112 covers the impeachment/confirmation institutional layer but not this nominee-toxicity rule | A nominee rejected at confirmation **automatically gains Controversial, then Incompetent** (becomes toxic/untouchable) and is **blocked from re-nomination** — automatic unless a blocking trait (Bookkeeper). Marked **ACCEPTED + already implemented in the 2022 forum game**. **★ SUPERSEDED (batch 31, `apptdeepdive` — the Sept-2022 DESIGN ORIGIN of the whole 2.3 confirmation process; this thread POSTDATES `fixes`'s Controversial→Incompetent draft and REPLACES it):** the **FINAL Ted-ruled fallout (with Cal's 9-historical-rejection analysis, POST 88-92) is NOT the Controversial→Incompetent cascade.** On a rejected/withdrawn nominee, roll: **33% the President is blamed → nominee gains `Controversial`; 33% the SML is blamed (politics) → nominee gains nothing; 34% nobody cares → no trait.** AND if the nominee **already had `Controversial`** and is denied → a **LIFETIME ban from Cabinet + Cabinet-Level roles** (may still serve as **Ambassador** or any no-confirmation role). So the prior "→ then Incompetent + total re-nomination block" cascade is replaced: the toxicity is **only Controversial (33% chance) + an already-Controversial-pol's lifetime Cabinet ban**, not an Incompetent escalation. **★ Human-canonical flag:** the open Q is which is newer — `fixes`/#199's cascade vs this 2022-final 33/33/34 rule. The deep-dive digest argues this 2022 thread describes the SAME forum game ("already implemented in the 2022 forum game") and is Ted's section-by-section FINAL lock of 2.3, so the 33/33/34 rule is the authoritative one unless a human confirms `fixes`'s cascade is a later re-revision | Add the confirmation-rejection fallout as the **33/33/34 blame roll → Controversial-or-nothing** + the **already-Controversial → lifetime-Cabinet/Cabinet-Level-ban (Ambassador still allowed)** rule (NOT the superseded Controversial→Incompetent cascade); keep the Bookkeeper carve-out only if a human re-affirms the older draft.
