Pairs with #136/#16/#18 | ingested (**ampuUpdates §4 N6 / POST 128; summer2021 POST 92-98, 74-80 (Celebrity merge/nerf + obscure-removal eligibility)**; **★ BATCH-34 (`kiaofficers` 68fa2220 POST 20-21) — Celebrity is EARNED, NOT SEEDED: even famous-by-heroic-death figures (Shaw, Custer) do NOT get a seeded `Celebrity` trait; like `Military Leader` (which vcczar REMOVED from every dataset fill — "that has to be earned"), Celebrity is acquired in play, never authored onto a `ROWS` entry. Corroborates the earned-not-seeded direction this expiry rule complements. kiaofficers POST 20, 21**; **★ BATCH-36 — `terminology` (b474593e) supplies the authoritative Celebrity DEFINITION ruling (vcczar POST 28/31, Ted POST 32): Celebrity = **NATIONWIDE recognition ONLY; it transcends a field** — war heroes, sports figures, in-field business/legal fame, and STATE-level fame do NOT qualify ("no paparazzi for war heroes"). Examples: Trump/PT-Barnum/Beyoncé = celebrity; Steve Largent / John Morgan / **Herschel Walker = NOT**. Origin: vcczar folded the old separate **"War Hero" trait INTO Celebrity** (same effect), created Celebrity mainly for Trump. ★ **earned-celebrity is ALLOWED but disliked** — "I allowed people to earn it even though I personally don't favor that" (direct corroboration of this earned/expiry row); house-rule precedent — Ted **STRIPPED Herschel Walker of Celebrity** in his 2022 playthrough. A proposed STATE-level "celebrity" tier (Walker @ UGA) was floated and NOT adopted. The trait name stays "Celebrity" ("Renown" rejected). terminology POST 27, 28, 31, 32, 39**) |
| 226 | **Frail / Hale auto-traits assigned by historical lifespan (died <60 ⇒ Frail; lived 86+ ⇒ Hale) — NEW (`ampuUpdates`; dataset rule)** | `Frail`/`Hale` are authored ad-hoc; no lifespan-derived auto-assignment rule in the dataset pipeline | **A dataset-generation rule (`ampuUpdates` POST 253-254).** **"Frail"** is auto-assigned to a pol who **died before 60**; **"Hale"** to one who **lived to 86+** (corrected up from 80). Drives the death/age-roll cluster (#36/#37) and is a dataset-authoring convention for `scripts/` (sits alongside the `draftYear`/sub-floor rules in CLAUDE.md). Author-side design data. Pairs with #36/#37 (age/death rolls) + the dataset pipeline | Add a lifespan-derived auto-trait pass to dataset generation: died <60 ⇒ Frail, lived 86+ ⇒ Hale. Pairs with #36/#37 + `scripts/` dataset pipeline | ingested (**ampuUpdates §4 N7 / POST 253, 254**; **★ BATCH-34 REFINEMENTS (two threads): (a) `strongnevernom` (326eee56) POST 34-35 — vcczar defines **Hale** = auto-assigned to any pol who lived past age **80** (helps avoid early death) and **Frail** = the opposite, for serious health problems / early natural deaths (e.g. LBJ); note this gives an **80** Hale threshold vs the **86+** in the ampuUpdates rule above — reconcile the cutoff (a death-timing modifier, ties #114/DH-36 mortality). (b) `kiaofficers` (68fa2220) POST 20-21 — ★ CRITICAL SCOPING: the lifespan rule keys on **NATURAL lifespan, NOT battle death** — a KIA who died young in combat but "could have lived to his 90s otherwise" is RULED **NOT Frail**; and `revolutionaryWar.ts` *grants* Frail (with a Hale resist roll, `:99-117`) on a battle WOUND — i.e. Frail is **earned in play**, not seeded onto a young battle death at birth. So the auto-assign pass must use the figure's natural/historical lifespan, and the wound-Frail mechanic is a separate in-play grant. Pairs with #36/#37 + `revolutionaryWar.ts:99-117`. strongnevernom POST 34, 35; kiaofficers POST 20, 21**) |
| 227 | **Trim-Roster phase REMOVED by the designer — random retirements handle roster pruning instead — NEW (`ampuUpdates`, rules delta)** | Reconcile vs shipped roster/retirement handling — verify whether a Trim-Roster step exists in `src/` | **A rules-structure delta (`ampuUpdates` POST 215).** vcczar **cut the Trim Roster phase**; **random retirements** now handle keeping the roster from bloating. The tech-lead must reconcile against the shipped phase loop / retirement handling (the death/retirement tuning in `summer2021` POST 66/174-176 — no random retirement <60, one-term-loser 50% retire, losing-nominee-<60 25% retire — is the companion ruleset that absorbs the cut phase). Pairs with the death/retirement cluster (#37) + `summer2021` retirement tuning | Confirm no Trim-Roster phase ships (or remove it); ensure random-retirement tuning (`summer2021` rates) does the roster-pruning the cut phase used to. Pairs with #37 | ingested (**ampuUpdates §4 N1 / POST 215; companion retirement tuning summer2021 POST 66, 174-176**) |

## Confirmed shipped bugs

**Defects in existing behavior + design holes** (roadmap = fixes, not features).
`BUG-*` are shipped-code defects (surfaced by `fed`, verified against the codebase
where quick); `DH-*` are **GM-confirmed rules gaps / design holes** from the forum
where the rulebook had no answer (these are design defects to spec, not crashes).

| # | Bug | Symptom | Root cause / status | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BUG-1 | **Era events don't deactivate for non-1772/1856 start years** | A scenario whose **start year is past an era** still has that era's events in the roll table, *and* (per the official ruling) events deactivate **only** if the start year is past the era — so e.g. an **1800-start game wrongly loses the Louisiana Purchase**. Stale events also dilute the roll table | The 1856 path calls `buildEraEventsForYear(year)` with **no era-vs-start-year filter** (phaseRunners.ts:2817). **Latent in the shipped build** (only 1772/1856 ship today) but a hard blocker the moment a federalism/1800 scenario is added. Wants an "era-lock" filter (unbuilt, fed posts 524, 535). Official ruling: `@Ich_bin_Tyler`, post 524 | ingested (fed 521-535; **rep1800 LIVE-CONFIRMS this exact bug: the GM found the Louisiana Purchase was listed under the prior Era of Federalism and so was “not included” for an 1800-start game; he hand-added it in 1816 — verbatim §A POST 2668. Independent same-class confirmation; DH-30 is the companion event-scheduler-min-floor fix**) |
| BUG-2 | **`Chisholm v. Georgia` lacks an "11th Amendment not ratified" gate** | The SCOTUS case should be gated on the 11th Amendment not yet being ratified | **Case not yet in the build** — no SCOTUS case data file contains it (grep: 0 hits in src). So this is a *forward requirement on the SCOTUS-case content*, not a live crash today. Logged to the dev's Basecamp by the forum | ingested (fed 145-150) |
| BUG-3 | **No fallback when there is no viable PM General candidate** | If no eligible politician exists for the PM General / `GeneralInChief` cabinet seat, the procedure is undefined → potential crash (player hand-waved with a "Hand of God" stat bump) | `GeneralInChief` is a real seat (types.ts:1121) gated by `cabinetSeatsForYear` (types.ts:1196), but the no-candidate path isn't covered. **Reported, crash-path unverified** — escalated to the dev (fed post 5) | ingested (fed 5, 119) |
| DH-1 | **A filibustered "MUST-pass" bill has no rules remedy** | The GM can declare a bill "MUST pass" (e.g. a required tariff each session); when the required tariff bill was **filibustered to death**, the rulebook had **no remedy**. The GM **improvised** a "special committee" of the 4 congressional leaders who must agree on a tariff that auto-passes, dropping EconStab + applying election penalties **per day until they agree** (an "AMPU government shutdown") | **GM-confirmed rules gap — VERIFIED in-thread** (GM explicitly flagged it to fix). The shipped engine needs a defined rule for a failed required/MUST-pass bill (deadlock-resolution: forced compromise, shutdown penalty clock, or fallback auto-pass) | ingested (modern 640, 696, 711, 716) |
| DH-2 | **Modern era-event deck appears decoupled from the literal year** | In the ~2018 turn the EraEvos deck pulled **2008-era cards** (Subprime Mortgage Crisis, ABM/INF treaties) — events fired years out of phase with the campaign clock | **Possible bug — REPORTED, not verified.** Could be intended shuffle/backlog or a scheduling defect; reconcile with BUG-1 (era-event scheduling/era-lock) and the era-event scheduling-model open question | ingested (modern 2221) |
| DH-3 | **Career-track pols can run for President** | A career-track pol is barred from Gov/Rep/leadership/Kingmaker but **no rule bars a presidential run** | **GM-acknowledged rules gap, intended-to-fix, unbuilt.** Bar career-track pols from the presidential candidate pool (and from CPU presidential selection) | ingested (hd 8205-8219; relates to #63) |
| DH-4 | **"Extend Credit to all nations" near-auto-win foreign loop** | Diplomacy "Extend Credit" is per-nation | **Balance flag:** extending credit to all 7 powers "works amazingly every time" — a positive trade balance with all nations triggers a stacked bonus (EconStab→Booming + random industry + random foreign relation). Needs a diminishing-returns / cap rule | ingested (hd 7346; relates to #26/#27) |
| DH-5 | **Kingmaker-flip grabs the protégé(s) — "insanely OP"** | Kingmaker/Protégé pairing exists (#design) | **Balance flag:** converting/flipping a Kingmaker also seizes his protégés (and their +1 election standing) — flagged "insanely OP." Needs a pairing-dissolution-on-flip rule (or no protégé transfer) | ingested (hd 7589, 8762; relates to #29/#30) |

| DH-14 | **Bill ideology impacts not era-aware** (★ REFRAMED batch 29: the "never passes" is a CPU-AI / era-ideology-weighting artifact, NOT an absolute mechanical block) | Bills carry fixed ideology effects | Matt (POSTS 6691, 6878, 6912): Mods need to be removed from the negative-points side of Women's Suffrage in 1916 — should be era-sensitive. Tyler agreed. **Equal Voting Rights for Women never passes** (60.5%, 63.6% short of 2/3); GM (all-CPU `drums`): *"This amendment will never pass in a game with CPUs."* Bills need era-keyed ideology impact tables. **★ REFRAME (`wilsons1916`, batch 29):** in a **human-majority 1916 game** the SAME "Equal Voting Rights for Women Amendment" **PASSES comfortably** — House **374-61**, Senate **79-17**, then ratified by states (VT the 36th, P383) → so the suffrage block is NOT a hard mechanical wall; it is a **CPU-vote-modeling + era-keyed-bill-ideology weighting** problem (the all-CPU `drums` field couldn't muster the 2/3 because Moderates sit on the negative side AND the CPU vote model under-supports it; humans with the same era mix pass it). The fix is therefore TWO things: (1) the era-keyed bill-ideology impact table (move Mods off the suffrage negative side in 1916, the original DH-14 ask), AND (2) the CPU vote model for amendments must be able to reach a 2/3 the way a human field does (`GM⇒App`, pairs with #114/E9/K5 + #208) | ingested (drums 6691, 6878, 6912; **★ wilsons1916 P383 — 19th Amendment RATIFIED in a 10-human 1916 game (House 374-61 / Sen 79-17), contradicting the `drums` all-CPU "never passes"; reframes DH-14 as a CPU-AI/era-weighting artifact**) |

| DH-29 | **Reconstruction Strict/Ironclad plan can essentially NEVER pass with CPU → solo Reconstruction unresolvable** | Reconstruction not in build (#57) | **★ Headline solo-play blocker (GM-VERIFIED).** `rep1800` POST 9170: *"the CPU factions will never vote for that bill… including red, only 3 factions would ever consider voting for it. GM names this a **primary driver of the in-progress CW/Reconstruction rules rewrite.** Any single-player antebellum/CW scenario inherits this — the historical-plan bill needs a solo-passable path (CPU default-vote bias for the historical plan, or a guaranteed-pass crisis path, or a re-spec). **Flag prominently for the roadmap.** **★★ `hd1` MOVEMENT (human-played confirmation + the FIX):** in the Part-1 run with **HUMANS on BOTH sides** of the Reconstruction tug-of-war (Southern-Dem wanting the 10% plan vs Radical-Rep wanting Ironclad/Mass-Trials), **the choice STILL deadlocked — neither plan passed and states drifted back into the Union with NO plan at all** ("The Congress could never agree on a Reconstruction guideline… in the end, neither passed," POST 2678). So the blocker is **structural, not a CPU-only artifact** (competing humans filibustered each other to the same null result). **The FIX is now designed (vcczar, #156):** ALL readmissions require **"a plan adopted by Congress OR by the President"** — the President can **unilaterally adopt** a plan, guaranteeing resolution in both solo and deadlocked-human play (POST 2693). **Build must implement the President-can-adopt-unilaterally rule.** | ingested (rep1800 §C 9166, 9170; **hd1 POST 2678, 2692-2694**; refines #57; FIX = #156) |
| DH-30 | **Era-event scheduler has a MAX per half-term but NO MIN floor** | Era-event scheduling not min-bounded (relates to BUG-1) | `rep1800` POST 2919–2932: events are scaled by a fixed NUMBER per era (over a 20-yr era a 25%-event ≈94% cumulative, 10%→65%, 5%→40%), but "the limit is a max not a min… which isn't what we discussed." **Agreed fix: minimum = 20% of the era's max (round down)**; if still none fire (all prereq-gated), fall back to the current 5 generic anytime events. A rejected alt (hard year-windows per event) was declined because *"events not happening every playthrough has been explicitly stated to be how the game operates"* (load-bearing for alt-history). **Companion to BUG-1.** | ingested (rep1800 §A 2918, 2919-2932; companion to BUG-1) |

| DH-78 | **★ Same-candidate TWO-TRAIT AND-combo election bonus (Celebrity AND Military Leader → +1) is NOT expressible in the shipped `TraitElectionRule` — NEW (`excelautomate`; verified against code)** | `TraitElectionRule` (`types.ts:727`) supports per-trait + per-`context` + signed `magnitude` + `era?` + an **opponent-conditional** swap (`ifOpponentHas` → `bumpedMagnitude`), and the `TRAIT_ELECTION_EFFECTS` table (`types.ts:738`) is consumed by `applyTraitElectionBonus` in `calcStateVote` (`phaseRunners.ts:3707`) — but there is **NO "candidate ALSO holds trait X" combo field**: a rule firing only when the SAME candidate holds two specified traits cannot be written | **A combo-bonus the spreadsheet GM built that the shipped rule shape can't represent (`excelautomate` 79fbbb46 POST 50).** Ted's election scorer used a VLOOKUP+COUNTIF combo to detect a candidate holding **both Celebrity AND Military Leader → +1** in elections — an explicit same-candidate two-trait AND-combo. The shipped `TraitElectionRule` prices each trait independently and can only condition on an OPPONENT's traits, so this combo is currently inexpressible. **Small / verify-before-building** — could have been intentionally dropped (the broader trait-vocabulary reconciliation #216 also touches `Military Leader`, which has no shipped union member yet); but logged because it is a concrete capability the rule TYPE lacks. Pairs with #189/#190 (the down-ballot trait stack), #216 (trait-vocabulary remap — `Military Leader` is one of the unmapped names), the #103 presidential modifier stack | Add a same-candidate trait-combo field to `TraitElectionRule` (e.g. `requiresAlsoHas: Trait[]` — fires only when the candidate holds ALL listed traits), or model combos as a small separate combo-rule table; first confirm `Military Leader`/`Celebrity` exist in the trait union (#216) and that the combo wasn't deliberately cut. Pairs with #189/#190/#216/#103 | codebase + ingested (**excelautomate (79fbbb46) POST 50; codebase-verified types.ts:727 `TraitElectionRule` has no same-candidate combo field, only `opponentConditional`; consumed at phaseRunners.ts:3707**) |
| DH-79 | **★ Naval battle results are RECORDED but NEVER consulted in the war win/loss check — the "one naval win ends naval forever" bug, confirmed in shipped code — NEW (`rethinkwar`; codebase-verified)** | `revolutionaryWar.ts` records `war.navalWins++/war.navalLosses++` after each naval engagement (`:202`), but the war-end check (`:254-264`) tests ONLY `war.currentGroundWins >= war.groundWinsNeeded` (=7) / `war.currentGroundLosses >= war.groundLossesRemaining` (=16, gated by `!war.frenchAlliance`) — naval tallies feed nothing | **The OP's complaint, confirmed in code.** MrPotatoTed (`rethinkwar` POST 1): *"winning one naval battle means you no longer have to worry about naval at all, even if the land invasion continues for another ten years."* Verified: the shipped 1772 engine fights at most ONE naval battle per phase (`:186-204`), increments `navalWins`/`navalLosses` (`:202`), but the win/loss decision (`:254-264`) is purely ground-count-based — so naval outcomes have **no bearing on whether the war ends**, naval never "continues to matter," and the French-alliance flag makes defeat impossible (`:259`). This is the concrete defect the #45 naval-as-difficulty-modifier redesign is meant to fix (naval persists every phase, FIRST, and shifts the land general's Mil ±1 instead of being a dead-end tally). As a standalone shipped bug it sits inside the broader count-based war-end model (#45) whose replacement is post-launch — so the immediate defect is "naval tally is dead code in the win check," fixable independently or as part of the #45 rewrite. Pairs with #45 (the redesign) + #56/#106 (generic war engine) | Either consult naval tallies in the war-end / difficulty math, or (preferred, per #45) replace the count-based win check with the War-Score model where naval persists and feeds land-battle difficulty (±1 Mil to the land general) rather than terminating after one win. Pairs with #45/#56/#106 | codebase + ingested (**rethinkwar (0fd0f2e5) POST 1, 16; codebase-verified `revolutionaryWar.ts:202` records navalWins/navalLosses, `:254-264` win-check uses only currentGroundWins/currentGroundLosses (+ `!frenchAlliance`), naval never read**) |
| DH-80 | **(verify-and-confirm) Election-scorer "Other racial" demographic term applied as a NEGATIVE in states where it should not be (e.g. Hawaii) — a possible SIGN error — NEW (`electiondisc`)** | Cal (`electiondisc` POST 31): *"'Other racial' shouldn't count as a negative in states like Hawaii."* Implies the election scorer applies a demographic/racial term to candidates that is mis-signed for non-mainland states (where "Other racial" is the majority, not a penalty) | **⚠ NOT confirmed in the shipped build — this is a SPREADSHEET-scorer observation.** Codebase-verified: there is NO race/ethnicity/"Other racial" term in `src/` (`grep -i 'racial\|ethnicit\|nonwhite'` over `src/` → only anytime-event copy, no scorer); the GENDER/demographics axis itself is unbuilt (#238/#239). **★ CORPUS-COVERAGE GAP (batch 30, `presidents` record).** The "Playtest Presidents"
record enumerates ~20 distinct forum playtests; **11 are ingested**, but **≥7 are NOT in
the corpus** and are named, ran for years, and are entirely absent — candidate future
uploads (ask the human if exports exist):

  the record (~100 in-game years, 27+ presidents)** with a **persistent Whig major party
  that never realigns** (a whole 1840 start scenario the shipped build has no analog for);
  marquee alt-history (Robert E. Lee AND Frederick Douglass both President; Granger = the
  community's best president, 3 terms). `presidents` POST 2, 31, 56, 75-76, 158-178.
- **1868-Bushwa** — Grant→Washburn→Cannon→Depew (Red Cloud = 1st Native VP); roster ≠
  ingested `gilded`/`gild1868`; "all 1-term Red" balance signal (POST 46-66).
- **1960-start** — Bricker def. JFK/Reagan; president ≠ ingested `redbutton` 1960 run →
  a distinct 1960 thread; defunct, CPU-revived as "1962" (POST 6, 9, 11).
- **2016-start** — Warner; the run that **drove the 2-Admin cabinet-minimum rule** (POST 44-45).
- **2024-start** — Haley→Inslee (Haley = 1st female president); ≠ ingested `trump2024`
  (setup-only) (POST 30, 35-37).
- **Three "old-forum" 1788 runs** + **an "old" 2000 run** (Bush-unlimited-terms→Biden) —
  pre-current-rules; likely unrecoverable but named in the record (POST 5, 12, 18, 21, 24).
- Balance topline (positive): the designer's cross-playtest read is **healthy party
  alternation** — never 3 same-party terms, never one-party-forever (POST 9-10); sub-signals
  (trait/command over-weighting "failing-upward" winners, weak early-era incumbency, frequent
  House-decided elections) feed #18/#184/#192/#214.

**★ CORPUS-COVERAGE UPDATE (batch 31, `bestmoments` cross-refs).** The "Best Playtest
Moments" highlights thread aggregates moments from MANY distinct playthroughs and re-confirms
which are un-ingested — sharpening the list above:
- **★ 1840-start (OrangeP47/Ich_bin_Tyler) — RECONFIRMED HIGHEST-VALUE missing upload.** The
  "1848 clustertruck" election (5 tied states + 6 faithless electors → 140-141-2, House
  contingency) — the single most-referenced moment in `bestmoments` (POST 4-5, 8) — is from
  this game; presidents run 1841→1873+ (Robert E. Lee President 1872, POST 153). Same game the
  `presidents` record flags as the longest-running (~100 yrs, persistent-Whig, never realigns).
  **Still absent from the corpus; the top future upload.**
- **matthewyoung123's GM'd 1772** (Senate-but-no-House; lifetime-term Presidency house rule) —
  drives the designer-authoritative "acting President" ruling (vcczar: a VP-turned-Pres under a
  lifetime-term amendment is acting only until the next election, does NOT inherit the lifetime
  term, can't shed "acting" via roll/exec-action; `bestmoments` POST 139-142, 146-147). **Check
  it has a digest** — distinct from the 7 ingested 1772 threads (a bespoke house-ruled
  convention). Pairs with #61/#112.
- **2012-start game** (Ron Paul wins the nomination, names his son VP; `bestmoments` POST
  127-129) — confirm this is one of the ingested 2012-start threads (`pop`/`pop2012b`) vs a
  distinct un-ingested run.
- Confirmed-already-ingested overlaps: the 1948 run = `nuke`; the 2016 "modern day" = `modernday`;
  a 1916 run = `solo1916`/`wilsons1916`; a 1868 Gilded run = `gilded`/`gild1868`; the Bartram/Cal
  rebooted-1772 + MrPotatoTed's 1772 solo overlap the founding-solo digests (verify same saves).
  No new era-band claims; `bestmoments` adds no architecture deltas (its value is the design-intent
  synthesis: the memorable moments come from the pre-12th EC/contingency/SCOTUS-challenge stack +
  succession/death/illness/scandal chains + per-2-yr skill/trait rolls reshuffling eligibility —
  the three loops the GM-subsume charter must keep producing).

  (GM @Bushwa777, a self-described rookie GM): poll → Gilded Age opening Jan 1869 (chosen for the

  signal: **multi-faction-per-player** is a forum-desired playtest mode (@pman runs 2 factions to
  stress-test it), adjacent to #114/DH-36. newplaytest POST 1, 15, 16, 26, 30-34.

## Sources

Sources are now split into **playtest threads** (continuous narrative threads
of an actual game-in-progress — the primary source for mechanics in play) and
**discussion threads** (community-curated fix-catalogs / rule-clarification
threads — secondary, but the primary source for **dataset accuracy**, small
mechanical bugs, and designer rulings on rules ambiguity).

### Playtest threads (ingested digests)

- **Ingested digests:**

### Discussion threads (community-curated catalogs; the dataset-accuracy source)

A *separate* class of source from the playtest threads. Discussion threads are
**not** game-in-progress narratives — they are running community-curated lists
of small fixes (dataset bugs, mechanical typos, designer-ruling clarifications)
that the build inherits as fix-it tickets, not as gameplay-validation. **Do not
confuse with playtest threads** — there are no GA rulings on a running game
here; there are designer rulings on policy/dataset Qs.

- [`cf82a7d3-a-thread-for-small-low-priority-changes-and-errors`](playtest-digests/cf82a7d3-a-thread-for-small-low-priority-changes-and-errors.md)
  (`smallbugs`) — **804 posts / 10 chunks** (single-pass reduce — a 3-year+
  community catalog of polish-tier fixes). Started Apr 2023 by @Imperator Taco
  Cat with the explicit charter "not… major changes to game rules or systems
  but fixing small errors"; ongoing through May 2026. The **primary source for
  dataset accuracy and small mechanical bugs.** Each entry is a one-line
  hand-off to the build, typically acknowledged within 1-2 reply posts by
  @MrPotatoTed, @vcczar, or @Arkansas Progressive and either "fixed inline" in
  the master sheet or deferred to "when Anthony codes that rule." **Headline
  contributions:** ~50 named-pol fixes, ~30 mechanical fixes, ~20 dataset
  additions (gap-log row **#120** umbrella) — all going via
  `scripts/seedDataset.mjs` `CURATED_ROWS` overrides; one NEW dataset gap
  (**#121 — Secessionist trait missing**); one NEW rules gap (**#122 — Pardon
  mechanics unspecified**); one late-modern content-fixes bundle (**#123**).
  **Designer-ruling distillate (§5 of digest):** Sept-2024 Ted batch of 8
  proposed rule changes (Pres-uses-Command-for-blunder hybrid adopted; Iron-Fist
  PL no-block / Disharmonious-or-Independent only-challenger gate adopted; etc.);
  **POST 734-735 is the channel through which the #38 relocation-cap-4 change
  was sent to Anthony for the build** (12-30-25, "Approved by vczar"). Strongly
  **corroborates DH-27 (trait-conflict slips in boot data, 3rd thread), DH-51
  (modern-pol overpowered recency bias, 3rd thread), DH-53 (bill→meter
  effect-table sign bugs, 4th thread), DH-60 (era-events fire without
  territory/asset prereqs, 2nd thread)**. Use as the **input catalog for one
  dataset-maintenance pass**.
